All of Europe Experiences Economic Panic 71

Switzerland Suffers from Too Much Gold

Canada Bans Gold Exports

National News Agency, Swiss Capital, 19th - At a time when all of Europe is suffering from economic panic, Switzerland alone is suffering from too much gold. Because apprehensive capitalists are depositing large sums in Swiss banks from countries such as Germany and England, the banks have no investment opportunities, so even long-term deposits do not earn interest. The total amount of long-term deposits has exceeded one billion Swiss francs, and gold from the United States continues to flow in. The managers of the banks are increasingly panicked.

Reuters, Ottawa, 20th - The Canadian government has issued an order that cash may not be exported from Canada unless authorized by the government. This ban will be in effect until March 1 next year and is intended to protect the gold standard, meet foreign debts, and maintain the legal banknote issuance reserve. It is found that Canada owes the United States several million dollars in principal and interest, which will soon be due.

Coal Mine Explosion in the Ruhr Area 72

National News Agency, Berlin, 19th - A coal mine explosion occurred in the Seni Mountain coal mine near Bochum in the Ruhr coal mining area. Eleven workers were killed and twenty-six were injured. After the mine explosion, all houses, worker headcount tables, etc. outside the mine were destroyed, so it is not possible to calculate the exact number of mine workers, but it is believed that it must be a considerable number, so rescue is still underway day and night. Furthermore, the Seni Mountain coal mine is the newest coal mine in the Ruhr area, and all the machinery, tools, etc. inside are the latest models, but it cannot avoid this disaster, which is truly lamentable and strange.

US Secretary of War Returns to San Francisco 73

Refuses to Discuss Philippine Independence

National News Agency, San Francisco, 19th - Secretary of War Hurley recently went to the Philippines to investigate the political, social, and economic situation. He has now completed his public service and returned to San Francisco today aboard the President Hoover. When reporters went to visit and inquire, Hurley only dealt with them briefly and refused to discuss the issue of Philippine independence. He will go to Washington within days to report the results of the investigation to President Hoover.

Important News

Important Foreigner's Report on Inspecting Liaoning and Jilin 74

There is No Truth to the Claim of Japanese Troops Withdrawing from Jilin

The Japanese Representative's Statement at the League of Nations is Entirely False

Beiping Correspondence: A certain important foreigner, concerned about the Northeast issue, personally went to various places in Liaoning and Jilin to inspect the truth. He was especially thorough in Jilin. Upon returning, he prepared a report, making an impartial record. The original text has already been sent overseas for publication. We have specially obtained a copy and translated it as follows:

"On the morning of September 19, the Japanese Second Battalion suddenly attacked the road police headquarters at the Erdaogou Station of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Chinese military camp at Nanling in Changchun. After a massacre in which 1,500 soldiers were killed, they occupied these two locations. Xi Qia, the acting chairman of Jilin Province and deputy commander of the Jilin Border Defense, upon receiving a report from Changchun, ordered the local Chinese military authorities not to retaliate against the Japanese army and sent two people to Changchun to investigate the incident. After the Jilin Provincial Government learned that Shenyang had also been attacked and occupied by the Japanese army on the night of the 18th, it convened a committee meeting to decide on a response. The committee ordered Shi Luben, the Jilin Foreign Affairs Director, to go to the Japanese consulate to inquire about the situation in Shenyang and Changchun. The Japanese consul immediately met with Xi Qia, the acting chairman of the Jilin Provincial Government, who inquired about the truth of the incident and the reasons for the Japanese army's attack. The Japanese consul replied that these were all military actions and beyond his knowledge. Before taking his leave, Xi Qia stated that, while the truth was unclear, the Chinese government would be responsible for protecting the lives and property of Japanese people in Jilin, and he hoped the Japanese consul would notify the Japanese authorities in Changchun not to send troops to Jilin City. The Japanese consul agreed to do so. On the 20th, in order to prevent the Chinese army from retaliating against the Japanese army due to the Changchun and Shenyang incidents, Xi Qia ordered the 25th Brigade and the 682nd Regiment of the Jilin Army, as well as the 11th Engineering Battalion, to move to the suburbs of Jilin. He sent Shi Luben to the Japanese consulate to inform the Japanese side of this matter, guaranteeing to the Japanese consul that the Chinese military police would fully protect the lives and property of Japanese people. On the same day, a telegram was received from the Jilin Japanese consul stating that the Japanese army in Changchun was prepared to go to Jilin on the 21st. Xi Qia then ordered the Chinese army to move further from its station. The purpose of the Chinese government's actions was, first, to avoid military conflict, and second, to comply with the Pact of Paris. On the 21st, two Japanese aircraft flew to Jilin for reconnaissance, dropping a large number of Japanese paper flags and various Chinese leaflets. The leaflets stated that the Chinese army in Shenyang had sabotaged the South Manchurian Railway at 10:30 p.m. on the 18th, killing and injuring several Japanese soldiers. The Japanese army had no choice but to use force to protect its vested rights in Manchuria. However, the truth is not so. According to official Chinese reports from Shenyang and those who witnessed the situation firsthand: (1) Shenyang was extremely quiet until 11 p.m., when the sound of gunfire was first heard. (2) At 11:15 p.m., the sound of an explosion was heard. The cause of the disturbance was that the Japanese themselves had sabotaged the Liuhe railway bridge on the South Manchurian Railway from Changchun to Shenyang. Therefore, the Japanese artillery stationed at the South Manchurian Railway Station bombarded the Beidaying barracks as their target. From this, we can know that the sabotage of the railway occurred simultaneously with or shortly after the Japanese army opened fire, and the Japanese used this as a pretext for military occupation of Manchuria. Judging from the Japanese security system on the South Manchurian Railway, no Chinese army could reach the railway area. How could they prepare to sabotage the railway without the Japanese knowing until the sabotage was successful? In fact, this matter is very simple, and for no reason, everyone knows the truth of this matter. On the same day, the Japanese army of the South Manchurian Railway dispatched three trains from Changchun to Jilin. Japanese and South Manchurian Railway personnel were stationed at each station to manage the railway. By dusk of that day, the entire route from Jilin to Changchun was under Japanese control, and all Chinese railway guards were disarmed. At 6:30 p.m., the Japanese army arrived at Jilin Station, forced their stay there until midnight. Then, the Japanese army entered the city, occupying the telegraph bureau, telephone bureau, radio station, arsenal, water company, electric light factory, military supplies depot, Bank of China, Jilin Provincial Bank, and all military institutions, police stations, and public institutions such as the Jilin Provincial Party Headquarters. All city gates and main streets were guarded by the Japanese army. Chinese infantry and cavalry were sent to all streets and alleys, and all incoming and outgoing pedestrians were thoroughly inspected. The Japanese army entering the city was the Second Division and the Third Company, with its headquarters located at the Japanese

Page 11

Important News

Taihe Hotel. Other Japanese troops were scattered inside and outside the city walls. On the 22nd, Japanese Commander Tamon ordered Xi Qia to disarm all Chinese troops leaving the city and ordered that the weapons be presented at noon on the 23rd, otherwise military action would be taken. The next day, Tamon ordered Japanese Colonel Tsuboi to become the chief of the Jilin Police Department, leading the disarmed Chinese police. After the reorganization of the police department, the following military rules were promulgated: (1) The Chinese police department is managed by Tsuboi. (2) Any Chinese police officers or soldiers who disobey the Japanese army and Japanese orders will be severely punished. (3) The Chinese police department will report to the Japanese military commander and arrest Chinese people who obstruct the actions of the Japanese. (4) The Chinese police should report to the Japanese military commander and arrest Chinese people whose actions endanger the safety of Japanese people in Jilin. (5) Chinese police who disobey the Japanese military commander and Japanese orders will be severely punished by military law. On the same day, Xi Qia collected more than a thousand rifles from the Jilin Military Academy and the 10th Brigade. The remaining Chinese troops in Jilin were not disarmed because they had already moved to the interior, and Xi Qia was unable to disarm all Chinese troops. Tamon imprisoned him in the Taihe Hotel, the Japanese army headquarters, with Japanese soldiers threatening him with guns for an hour. At the same time, the Japanese military commander put forward the following conditions for Xi Qia to accept: (1) Reorganize the provincial government. (2) Dissolve the provincial committee. (3) Appoint a new civil and military leader. (4) Abolish the committee system. (5) Adopt the dictatorship of the civil and military leader. Under the above circumstances, Xi Qia was forced to agree at that time. Tamon then turned his anger into a smile, and the matter of disarming the Chinese army was delayed. Thereupon, the Japanese forcibly obtained the right to rule Jilin from the Chinese authorities, and with Colonel Tsuboi as their representative, used the power of bayonets to direct government affairs. On September 23rd and 24th, looting took place in Jilin. All the field guns, light and heavy military vehicles, and important and valuable items stored in the Jilin Arsenal were looted. On the 25th, the Japanese Third Company returned to Changchun, and the 15th Company went to Jilin to replace them. The Japanese army distributed themselves throughout Jilin City as follows: (1) The 15th Company resides in the South Manchurian Railway dormitory in Baocheng Hutong, East City. (2) The 30th Squad resides in the Jilin Military Department. (3) The First Team resides in the Jilin Provincial Department. (4) The First Company is the same as above. (5) The Second Company resides in the Military Supplies School at the Sandao Wharf. (6) The Third Company resides in the Jilin Military Department. (7) The Machine Gun Team is the same as above. (8) The 16th Squad Headquarters resides in the Japanese Laixing Hotel in East City. (9) The Second Team resides in the South Manchurian Railway Detective Agency. (10) The 15th Company resides in Japanese residences in East City. (11) The Sixth Company is the same as above. (12) The Seventh Company is the same as above. (13) The Machine Gun Company is the same as above. (14) The Third Team is the same as above. (15) The Ninth Company is the same as above. (16) The Tenth Company is the same as above. (17) The Eleventh Company is the same as above. (18) The Machine Gun Company is the same as above. (19) The Field Artillery Team resides next to the Laixing Hotel. (20) The Cavalry Team resides next to the foreigner, Klein. (21) The Guard Team resides in the Hengmao Flour Mill. On October 5th, more than 500 Japanese troops returned from Dunhua, the end point of the Jidun Railway. This team was dispatched to Dunhua on September 23rd. After returning to Jilin, they were stationed in various important areas inside and outside the city. The Japanese troops installed running water and telephones wherever they lived. The Japanese army also dug trenches along the Jichang Railway and erected cannons on Xihuanxi Mountain, Beihuanxi Mountain, and the Dongjiang Bridge. Recently, the Japanese army established a 3,000 square foot airfield on the left bank of the Songhua River, east of Jilin City and north of the Jichang Road, 1.5 miles away, regardless of who owned the land and the unharvested crops of poor farmers. With the Japanese army's full military preparations, everything in Jilin is in their hands. Under the rule of the Japanese army, the Japanese began to plunder everything they had long desired, treating Jilin and other parts of Manchuria as the second Korea, regardless of all previous international treaties, China's sovereignty in Manchuria, and the Japanese representative Yoshizawa's statement at the League of Nations that no matter what recent military actions took place, the Japanese had no intention of aggression. Violating all faith, they will complete a permanent occupation through military occupation. On September 30th, the chief of the Japanese Police Department ordered Xi Qia to abolish the Deputy Military Department and the Jilin Provincial Government organization. On the same day, the Japanese established a Japanese-style military and political office with Xi Qia as a puppet. Under the supervision of Tsuboi, the chief of the Japanese Police Department, and Tamon, the Japanese commander, an inauguration ceremony was held. During the inauguration ceremony, Xi Qia and the two Japanese people on either side of him, as well as the audience, were photographed by Japanese reporters. The Japanese side intended to separate Jilin from the Chinese central government and establish a protected government under the command of the Japanese army. This can be proven by the local governments currently established. Since the Japanese army arrived in Jilin, the following actions have taken place: (1) All Chinese gatherings are strictly prohibited. (2) The publication of all Japanese military actions is strictly restricted. (3) All privately owned firearms allowed by Chinese law are confiscated. (4) People traveling on the streets from 7 p.m. to 5 a.m. are strictly inspected. (5) Chinese-dressed Japanese detectives are spread throughout the city. (6) All Korean prisoners, regardless of their crimes, are released. (7) Anti-Japanese Koreans are arrested. It is rumored that six people have been shot and killed by the Japanese. (8) The Japanese army and Japanese aircraft are distributed throughout the suburbs and other areas every day, and many tragedies have occurred. (9) Han Jingyuan (transliteration), the director of the Chinese military law office, was arrested and imprisoned in the Japanese consulate because Han ruled against Korean prisoners against the will of the Japanese. (10) Shi Luben, the Chinese Foreign Affairs Director of Jilin, was ordered to leave Jilin within five days for failing to salute the Japanese military commander. (11) All Chinese people are not allowed to use telegrams. (12) The Japanese army destroyed the radio station, making it unusable. (13) Ten days ago, the Japanese military commander seized 200,000 yuan in cash from the Jilin Provincial Treasury and ordered the Chinese treasurer not to disclose it. (14) The residences of important people in Dongguan were all looted, and all valuables were taken away. (15) All books by Sun Yat-sen and pamphlets of the Kuomintang were arrested and confiscated. Pictures of Sun Yat-sen were also confiscated. (16) The Japanese army ordered those carrying books in the streets to stop and be thoroughly inspected before being released. (17) The Japanese army paid special attention to school teachers, male and female students, and often entered girls' schools. (18) Before the arrival of the American consul and his staff, most of the Japanese army retreated to Lianhuabao to avoid displaying a large army at the city gates and streets. (19) Every day, the Japanese army patrols the streets and alleys of the city to collect materials in preparation for compiling a military map of Jilin City and its suburbs. (20) The Japanese military commander recently forced Xi Qia, the so-called Chinese governor of Jilin Province, to hire three Japanese people, one as a technical and political advisor to the provincial government with a monthly salary of 800 yuan, and two with a monthly salary of 300 yuan. Although their actual responsibilities in the provisional government have not yet been made public, they are nothing more than supervising the current government. (21) Yesterday morning, the police department announced that the Japanese army would conduct artillery drills from October 11 to 17, from 9 a.m. to 12 p.m. and from 1 p.m. to 3 p.m. every day. Cannons were set up in Dongdatan with the old gunpowder bureau as the target. In addition to the above actions, the Japanese army occupied Tongliao, Xinmin, Yingkou, Niuzhuang, Taonan, and Yingpan in addition to occupying Shenyang and Changchun. The above locations were all occupied after the Japanese representative declared at the League of Nations that the Japanese government had begun to withdraw Japanese troops outside the South Manchurian Railway. Jilin and the other locations mentioned above are all far from the South Manchurian Railway. In any case, according to previous treaties, the Japanese had no right to station troops in the above locations. We do not know on what legitimate grounds the Japanese sent troops to the above locations, but the Japanese intend to sabotage the Manchurian railways in order to obtain a monopoly on Northeast transportation for the South Manchurian Railway. The above locations are the intersections of important railways. The above is an accurate report of the Japanese army's activities in Jilin, obtaining control of the Jilin government, preparing for or currently preparing for the permanent occupation of Jilin, violating the official international statements of Japanese diplomats, the shameful behavior of Japanese officials and soldiers, inhumane measures, and painstakingly avoiding publicizing the facts to the world. China, Japan, and other civilized countries are all signatories to the Kellogg-Briand Pact, which is an instrument for maintaining world peace. China has submitted this case to the League of Nations for a fair resolution. Due to limited space, we fully state the factual facts. All my readers, with their own impartial opinions, should assist in eliciting international public opinion to oppose any country that attacks another country regardless of all international laws and customs, so that we can guide the world to lasting peace."

Yuan Jinkai Discusses the Shenyang Incident 75

The Japanese Forced Him to Form an Independent Government

Refused Zhang's Return to Shenyang and Separation from the Central Government

He Has Expressed His Rejection of This Move

Tianjin News: Recently, two German journalists, accompanied by An Dake, visited Yuan Jinkai, the chairman of the Liaoning Local Maintenance Committee, in Shenyang for a lengthy discussion. Although much of what Yuan said was self-justification, he did not conceal the fact that the Japanese forced him to form an independent government. The following is An's record of the conversation between the two parties: The German journalists arrived at the Shenyang Local Maintenance Committee at 2 p.m. on the 15th of this month. Wang Rujiu had made prior arrangements. After submitting their calling cards, they were received by Yuan. After exchanging greetings, the German journalists first stated their intentions and their experiences in Jilin and Harbin, and wanted to know the recent situation and changes in Liaoning. Yuan said frankly: "Since this unfortunate incident occurred suddenly, our officials, soldiers, and police have all left the provincial capital and fled. I (Yuan refers to himself) was originally a scholar, and could have gone elsewhere at that time, but I couldn't bear to see my hometown suffer again, so I acted out of my personal conscience and organized the Maintenance Committee. I usually interacted with the Japanese, and had many old friends. This time, the organization of the Maintenance Committee was not opposed by the Japanese. Now the Liaoning provincial capital is much quieter than it was a few days ago. As for the overall situation, I would like to tell you all about it. The Japanese have come to persuade me about forming a new government, but I have insisted that I do not want an independent government to be established, so I have established this Maintenance Committee to support this situation. But it is temporary in nature. I will do my best in the Maintenance Committee for as long as it lasts. As for the various institutions that must be established, they have now been newly established. The Japanese have also placed advisors in various institutions, who will withdraw as soon as the new government is established. I have not signed anything for any matter, nor have I recognized any conditions on their part. The Japanese do not want Deputy Commander Zhang to return, not because they do not want Marshal Zhang to return, because he is a military man, nor do they want Chairman Zang to return to office, because he is an official. The Japanese think that I am a local gentleman in Fengtian and can organize an independent government, but I have refused. I will use an analogy. Fengtian is like a large family. The head of the family is away and has not returned. The uncles and brothers of the head of the family can be responsible for everything. The Marshal can be compared to an uncle, and Chairman Zang can be compared to a brother, and I am the teacher of the family, who can only watch over the house while the master is away and cannot rule in his place. Therefore, at this time, if anyone takes anything from the house, I will only watch. The Japanese know that I do not want to organize a new government, so they have not forced me. However, the organization of the Maintenance Committee can only muddle through for a while. It is feared that there will be changes over time, or that a third party will succeed me and organize a new government. But the Japanese cannot force me to become independent now. During this period of no government, some unscrupulous people want to take the opportunity to cause trouble. In my personal opinion, the Japanese do not want young Marshal Zhang to return here. According to the Japanese, the Japanese killed Marshal Zhang, so suspicion and emotion are naturally incompatible. But the Japanese also do not want the Nanjing government to send personnel here. The Japanese do not want to have any relationship with the National Government, but they do not intend to take away the three eastern provinces immediately. The Japanese intend to establish an independent new government under Japanese supervision, with a majority of Japanese officials. Wouldn't that become the second Korea?"

(German journalist): "In your opinion, how long will it take to come to an end?"

(Yuan replied): "I initially thought that the negotiations could be completed within one or two months. If the Japanese insist on establishing an independent new government, then I dare not say how long it will take. In short, I sincerely hope that our authorities will find a way to resolve this matter as soon as possible. At present, the Japanese know that no one is willing to organize a government, and many Japanese ronin have gone to the Mongolian border to promote independence. This is really worrying. The Japanese know that Chiang and Zhang are planning to declare war on Japan. The Japanese have long been prepared and say that if Japan wins the war, it will definitely take the three eastern provinces."

(Journalist): "Is there any news that Commander Kan Du is organizing a government?" (Yuan replied): "Kan is also very concerned about the local establishment of the Maintenance Committee, but the Japanese have a slightly worse feeling towards him, so it was merged with our Maintenance Committee and he was invited to be the deputy director. As for the level of organizing a government, he may not be willing to do it now."

(Journalist): "Is it Wang Xiaobo (Chengbin) who was invited out by the Japanese to organize a government?"

(Yuan replied): "Xiaobo is a very good person and very talented. He has always lived in Dalian. There is no news of Wang coming here for this kind of thing."

(Journalist): "Is Zhang Zongchang also active on their side?"

(Yuan replied): "Zhang Zongchang is not from Fengtian. His reputation in Shandong was very bad. The Japanese once came here to seek my opinion. I said that if Japan has no intention of harming the three eastern provinces, there is no need to invite him out."

(Journalist): "How has the industrial and commercial industry been since the incident?"

(Yuan replied): "Of course, it is not as good as before, but from today onwards, the three eastern provinces' official silver companies and Bianye banks have resumed business, which is very good for local finance. I once declared that the reason why I came out to maintain the local area is to reduce the suffering of the people. I let people laugh and scold me."

(Journalist): "I heard that the Shenyang-Zhangjiakou Railway has been opened to traffic, is that true?"

(Yuan replied): "This road has been opened to traffic because food can be transported from the north. There are also Japanese people in the railway bureau. The Japanese side requires all institutions to open and place people inside to monitor them. Only the mayor of the municipal office is a Japanese person. The rest of the office is headed by a Chinese person. Since the leader is a Japanese person, all affairs should be the responsibility of the Japanese." (Journalist): "When will schools start? Do you know if the Northeast University factory has started construction? Also, how will the official shares of the Shenyang-Hai Railway be handled?" (Yuan replied): "It is too early to talk about school. I don't know about the construction of the factory. I heard that the official shares of the Shenhai Railway have been taken by the Japanese."

(Yuan asked the journalist): "Did you meet with Director Xi in Jilin?"

(The journalist replied): "I didn't meet him, only Secretary Zhang met with him on his behalf."

Yuan said that Jilin is a special situation different from Fengtian. Xi is the deputy marshal and the acting civil and military officer in charge, so there is the matter of organizing a government. I am not like that. It is not appropriate to organize a government in Fengtian without Chairman Zang's consent. If the Japanese insist on asking me to organize a government, it would be okay in the short term for the sake of the overall situation, but if we become permanently independent and participate in many Japanese officials, wouldn't that be the same as Korea, being protected by Japan and being slaves of a subjugated country? Now it is a case of "having officials but no people." This time, the personnel of all important institutions were all invited by me. They were all unwilling to take office at first. I said that there is no problem with doing things, and one person will bear the burden, which has nothing to do with the public."

(Yuan asked): "How is the situation in Harbin?"

(The journalist replied): "Harbin and Heilongjiang both obey Commander Zhang, but the finances are slightly chaotic."

Yuan said that he had just received news that the finances were better than before. A few days ago, the local finances were also very chaotic. From today onwards, it will only cost six yuan to remit Tianjin silver dollars per hundred yuan. If you use one yuan locally, it will be counted as one yuan without any discount. In the past twenty days, my important work has been to recruit two thousand self-defense police and six hundred security guards. The Japanese have returned a small number of guns, and local order has gradually been restored. Since then, businesses and banks have also resumed operations one after another, and the court will also open. The Japanese have not asked to send officials to join, and the Japanese also know that the judiciary is independent."

The journalist said that he had met with the Marshal in Jin County. At that time, the situation in Jilin was still good, and the Marshal instructed us to go and see them so that they could work with peace of mind.

Yuan said that the Marshal had also sent people to contact me and told me that I could come forward to maintain the situation as I saw fit, but I was very unwilling to establish more institutions. The Japanese had asked the Finance Department to handle it separately. I said, "How can there be another Finance Department in Jinzhou?" The Japanese said that they could expel it and dissolve it. Unexpectedly, Jinzhou was bombed later.

(Yuan asked): "Why did the Beining Railway stop for a day?"

(The journalist replied): "The Japanese transported three thousand people to the Liaohe River, claiming to suppress bandits. It is now open to traffic."

The Japanese Also Request the Extension of the Chongqing Japanese Concession 76

Threatening Liu Xiang with Gunboat Diplomacy

Chongqing Correspondence: Since the bad news of the Japanese army's invasion and occupation of the Northeast spread, the people of Jiangba have been extremely indignant. The military, government, and party have all been busy holding meetings to discuss countermeasures. Although the specific measures are pending negotiation, the determination to unite against Japan is generally visible. Liu Xiang was even more激烈的 because he was intimidated by the written letter of the Japanese Consul General in Chongqing, Aono Chotaro. The anti-Japanese atmosphere in Chongqing was once tense because the people were eager to recover the Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession. Because of repeated telegrams from Nanjing instructing the people not to cause other troubles, the people of Sanba, although they had a direct proposal to recover it, returned to silence. Recently, the people have arisen again because the Japanese army has occupied the territory of the Northeast. The Japanese consul has repeatedly sent letters to Liu Xiang requesting him to stop this, and three warships have been transferred from Hanyi, one of which has arrived and the others will arrive to carry out armed preparedness in the name of protecting the Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession. Recently, Consul Aono also sent a letter to Liu Xiang requesting the renewal of the Wangjiatuo Concession agreement, limiting the time for signing, otherwise, he would not be responsible for any major changes. According to the brief history of the Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession, after the Sino-Japanese War in the 20th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty (1894 AD), the Treaty of Shimonoseki was agreed to allow Japanese merchants to trade in Sichuan. After the Japanese arrived in Chongqing, they saw that the products of Sichuan Province were abundant and they were very envious. They used the excuse that there were more and more overseas Chinese and leased land for residences to facilitate special management. The Qing officials did not know what national rights were. In the 22nd year of Guangxu, the Chongqing Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession land base was agreed. In the 27th year, the Sichuan Governor-General and Acting General Kui Jun (Manchu) in Chengdu sent the Sichuan Eastern Military Preparation Dao and concurrently handled commercial affairs. Bao Fen and Yamazaki Kei, the Japanese consul stationed in Chongqing, finalized all matters relating to the concession. The public used the name of the public welfare office to purchase private land and demarcated a length of 100 zhang and a width of 105 zhang and 2 chi as the Japanese concession. A thirty-year return agreement was signed, totaling 22 articles, entitled "Chongqing Japanese Merchants' Special Concession Agreement." Counting on fingers, this year has reached the end of the thirty-year period. The people of Jiangba hold this reason and are eager to recover the entire territory. Therefore, the Japanese first coerced the Chongqing authorities to continue to sign an agreement in order to deal with Liu Xiang, who said that this matter should be decided by the central government. The local officials under the rule of the National Government do not have the power to sign treaties. At the same time, the people were very indignant and held a citizens' meeting on the 28th to support the government's diplomacy.

Earlier, the people of Jiangba had long been prepared to automatically recover the Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession on the south bank of Chongqing because it was about to expire. Recently, the relationship between China and Japan has deteriorated due to the major changes in the Northeast. Aono Chotaro, the Japanese consul stationed in Chongqing, feared that the people would actually rise up automatically, which would inevitably lead to many misunderstandings. He visited Liu Xiang a few days ago and asked for a solution. Liu refused to see him because he was busy, so he returned to his office in disappointment. On the 21st, he sent an official letter to the 21st Army Headquarters, saying that the Wangjiatuo Japanese Concession was officially leased by the Chinese government in the 26th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, not occupied by itself. Now, although the term has expired, additional rent can be paid. If it is to be recovered, it must wait until Chinese law is effective and judicial reforms have a definite guarantee for foreign residents before it can be discussed. Now I hear that the Jiangba rogues will carry out barbaric actions to automatically recover it, and I ask you to stop it to avoid accidents. Otherwise, the Japanese warships in Chongqing will fear that an unfortunate event will occur for self-defense, etc. After reading it, Liu, in addition to ordering the Baxian government to pay attention to prevention, immediately telegraphed the central government to request instructions. (September 30)

Petitions to the National Government from Beijing's Academic Circles 77

Seven Points Proposed

Received by Kong Xiangxi

On the 20th, at 8 a.m., all schools in the capital held a citywide student assembly at the Zhongnan Middle School playground in Shibanqiao. More than 10,000 students from National Central University, Jinling University, and various middle and primary schools attended. After the chairman, Yuan Qijiong of National Central University, presided over the ceremony, the chairman first reported the significance of the meeting, followed by a discussion of the following proposals: (1) Promote peaceful unification; (2) Oppose direct negotiations before the Japanese troops withdraw; (3) Severely punish traitors; (4) Intensify military preparations to fight for world justice; (5) Restore popular movements; (6) Issue firearms to volunteer soldiers; (7) Implement a steel industry policy. All were unanimously passed on the spot. Finally, a declaration and two telegrams, one to the League of Nations and one to Shi Zhaoji, were approved. The meeting then adjourned and the participants formed a procession to demonstrate. National Central University and Jinling University served as the chief and deputy commanders. The procession first went to the National Government to petition. Fifteen members of the assembly's presidium entered the government to request an audience with Chairman Chiang. Chiang sent Kong Xiangxi and Minister of Education Li Shuhua to meet with them. The representatives stated their intentions and then presented their petition, requesting a response to the public. Kong agreed and accompanied the representatives to the front of the National Government's gate to address the crowd. He said, in essence, that the purpose of your studies is to serve the country and society after graduation, to make the country prosperous and the people happy in accordance with the Principle of People's Livelihood. Since Japan forcibly occupied the Eastern Provinces, you have continued to study as usual, but you have never forgotten your patriotic movement. This patriotic enthusiasm is enough to wash away the shame of "five minutes of heat" on the one hand, and to urge the government to strengthen diplomacy with the strength of the people on the other. Government colleagues are very pleased with your actions, because the government is a government for the people, and should rely on the people for support. Without the support of the people, the government cannot show its strength. You are all intellectuals, and such patriotism gives China great hope for the future. Regarding the seven points you requested: (1) To promote peaceful unification, the Guangdong representatives have already departed from Hong Kong for Shanghai. Last night, representatives of the central comrades also went to Shanghai to welcome and negotiate with them. Within two or three days, they will come to Nanjing to cooperate and achieve peaceful unification. Today, you listed this matter as the first, which shows your eagerness for peace. I think that the representatives will see this and be able to sacrifice everything to share the responsibility of saving the country; (2) There must be no direct negotiations before the Japanese troops withdraw. The National Government has decided that no matter how Japan oppresses us, we will never negotiate if the Japanese troops do not withdraw. Please rest assured on this point; (3) Severely punish traitors. In the past, because rewards were more numerous than punishments, traitors often escaped punishment, so that they were not afraid. In the future, if there are any more traitors, the government will punish them according to the law to satisfy the public; (4) Intensify military training to fight for world justice. Since the Mukden Incident, not only soldiers have been waiting in readiness, but the people are also willing to sacrifice for the country. This shows the patriotic enthusiasm of the people. Chairman Chiang recently stated that China is not only a member of the League of Nations, but also a signatory to the Kellogg-Briand Pact. If anyone does not uphold justice, China is willing to sacrifice everything to uphold justice. This is the determination of the Central Government, which I can tell you; (5) Restore popular movements. Since the suppression of the communists, there have been some restrictions on popular movements due to various reasons, but they are not absolutely prohibited. The government welcomes orderly actions like yours today; (6) Issue firearms. The government has already instructed the Directorate General of Training to plan everything. If there is a real need in the future, the government will issue them; (7) Implement a steel industry policy. The government and the Ministry of Industry are already planning this matter, which is extremely important to the development of industry in the future. The government will pay attention to it. Kong also said that in the past, foreigners considered China to be a sleeping lion, and some even said that China was like a sheet of loose sand. Looking at China's situation today, we can wipe away the shame of this statement. I still hope that you will take today's patriotic spirit back to your hometown and awaken the people to unanimously support the government. Then, there is nothing to fear. After Kong's speech, the students marched and demonstrated according to the planned route. Military music led each team, and slogans were shouted along the way. Leaflets were distributed. The onlookers on both sides were extremely crowded. After 1 p.m., they arrived at the Central Party Headquarters to petition. Ding Weifen, Chen Lifu, Cheng Tianfang and others responded separately before they returned to their schools.

Anti-Japanese Grand Parade by Academic Circles in Wuhan 78

Held Separately in Wuchang and Hanyang

Declaration Issued by the Anti-Japanese General Association

A HanKou dispatch reports that to resist the violent Japanese and save the country from danger, the academic circles of Wuhan organized the Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association in Wuchang and held a parade and demonstration on the 19th in Wuchang and Hanyang to promote the attention of all sectors of the public. In Wuchang, a total of more than 10,000 people from 37 schools gathered at the Yue Ma Factory. At 9 a.m., a meeting was held to appoint Wu Yutian, a representative of Wuhan University, as the general chairman, and Xiong Wu of the Police Academy as the general commander. First, the chairman reported the significance of the meeting, and then the general commander reported the parade route and order. The parade started with universities and colleges as the first group, primary schools as the second group, and middle schools as the third group. Four students from the Police Academy served as guides, and two students from the Police Academy served as marshals in each team. After departing from the Yue Ma Factory, the parade passed through Da Chao Street, Bao'an Gate, Zhimailing, Lanling Street, and turned to Hanyang Gate, where the teams dispersed. The parade was very orderly, with participants shouting slogans along the way. In Hanyang, more than 1,000 people from more than 10 schools gathered at the large playground of the Provincial No. 12 Middle School at 9 a.m. The director of moral education of the Provincial No. 3 Middle School was appointed as the general commander. After the meeting, the teams were organized and departed from there, passing through Hanyang Main Street to Ximenkou, turning to the area near Turtle Mountain, and the teams dispersed at 12 noon. At 1 p.m., Wuchang and Hanyang simultaneously carried out a general anti-Japanese propaganda campaign. All schools dispatched lecturers to deliver impassioned speeches on the conspiracy of Japanese aggression against China and the tragic situation of the ravaging of the three northeastern provinces, hoping that all compatriots would rise up together to seek self-rescue as soon as possible. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association issued a declaration advocating four things: (1) Arming the entire population and actively preparing for war; (2) Thoroughly severing economic relations with Japan; (3) Promoting the peaceful unification of the country; (4) Expanding the anti-Japanese national salvation organization. A telegram was sent to the Central National Government, requesting preparation for a declaration of war against Japan, and a telegram was sent to the whole country to concentrate efforts and fight to the death. The original telegram read: (1) Respectfully submitted to the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters and the National Government: It has been nearly a month since the violent Japanese forcibly occupied Liaoning and Jilin. Our government and people have maintained calm and restraint and have not resisted, but the atrocities of the Japanese army have increased. Recently, they have bombed Jinzhou and increased their ships inland, shocking the world and angering the whole country. Although the League of Nations has convened two meetings, judging from past precedents, it is expected that there will be no effect. At this time, when the nation is in imminent danger, we must quickly decide on a plan to survive to the death. The association unites the Wuhan academic circles and vows to do its best to resist Japan from beginning to end. We respectfully request that the Ministry and Government make preparations for a declaration of war with the greatest determination. The opportunity for survival is at hand. With tears, we respectfully submit this telegram for your consideration. Respectfully, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association of Wuhan Academic Circles. (2) Respectfully submitted to all compatriots across the country: It has been a month since the violent Japanese forcibly occupied Liaoning and Jilin. Their barbaric acts continue unabated. While we suppress our voices and swallow our tears, we truly cannot bear the pain of self-humiliation. Over the years, the people of the country have merely indulged in emotions and party divisions have been divergent. Politics have deteriorated day by day, and the people's livelihood has become increasingly difficult. Internal strife has not been quelled, and external troubles have come. The nation is in danger at this time more than ever before. The association unites the Wuhan academic circles to face the national crisis and save the country by resisting Japan. We only rely on our strength. We hope that all compatriots across the country will be aware of the danger and eliminate all private opinions. Thoroughly awaken and sincerely unite. Gather the strength of the entire nation to fight to the death with the Japanese pirates. With blood, we present these words for your wise consideration. Respectfully, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association of Wuhan Academic Circles. (October 19th)

Local Correspondence

Changshu 79

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association is Obstructed. Since its establishment, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this county has seized quite a few Japanese goods in recent days. It is now trying to persuade shops to seal up their stockpiles of Japanese goods. Unexpectedly, a party member, Dai Huidong, went to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association on the 19th and demanded that 30 bags of white sugar that had been seized earlier be returned. Dai is the owner of Hengsheng Store, which imported the sugar. He claimed that it was Taikoo sugar and not Japanese sugar. The chairman of the Anti-Japanese Association, Shen Zuguang, said that the goods had the Tai Chi trademark, which was undoubtedly enemy goods according to the comparison table. Now that it is claimed to be Taikoo goods, there is still suspicion. He is currently attaching a sample and requesting the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association to identify it. Please be patient. Unexpectedly, Dai did not listen and began to roar. He also ran around to negotiate with the Anti-Japanese Association's committee members and the party branch's committee member, Li Junyuan, asking for the goods to be returned. It is said that Committee Member Li seemed to agree, and the Anti-Japanese Committee member, Lu Gongquan, volunteered to go to Shanghai with the Chamber of Commerce staff to inquire in the hope of having Dai reclaim the goods. However, before long, it had spread throughout the community and was opposed by the public. This plan was thus rejected.

Japanese National Discovered at Dayi Bridge. Dayi Bridge Town, located more than ten li north of this county, is a densely populated area and an important passage connecting with Jiangyin. Unexpectedly, a Japanese national was discovered there on the 19th wearing Chinese civilian clothes and wandering the streets. The villagers noticed him and gathered around to watch. Some said that this person was a Japanese spy or had come from Jiangyin to investigate the situation. According to someone, this Japanese person was a relative of a Zhou family in the town, but at this time of national emergency, the sudden arrival of this Japanese person cannot help but arouse suspicion.

Wuxi 80

Verdict on the Case of Forcible Intercourse with a Young Girl. The case of Bian Jinlong, a tailor worker in Cangbangli outside the west gate of this county, who forcibly engaged in sexual intercourse with A San, the daughter of his cohabitant Jiang Xingzhu, has been investigated and concluded by the Procuratorate and prosecuted. Judge Huang opened a court session to interrogate and set a date for sentencing. At 10 a.m. yesterday, Judge Huang ascended to the second court and summoned Bian Jinlong to the court. After a brief interrogation, he stood up and read the judgment: Bian Jinlong was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for forcible intercourse with an underage girl and deprived of his civil rights for ten years. The unresolved detention days are allowed to be offset against the imprisonment term at the rate of two days for one day. After the judgment was pronounced, he was returned to custody to await the expiration of the appeal period before being sent to prison for execution.

Date Set for Sentencing in the Case of Beating a Senior Relative to Death. Zheng Chunquan, a villager from Zhengjia Alley near Doumenli in the 16th district of the county, used a dry tobacco pipe to beat his father, Zheng Genda, on the left corner of his forehead last month. The next day, his father died of serious injuries. Prosecutor Du went to the village to open the coffin for an inquest and took Zheng Chunquan into custody. Recently, the prosecutor filed a public prosecution. Yesterday (the 20th) at 5 p.m., Judge Huang opened a court session to question Zheng Chunquan. The testimony of Zheng Chunquan and his mother, Zhang, differed greatly. Judge Huang ordered that he be punished in accordance with the second half of the first paragraph of Article 298 of the Criminal Law and scheduled the sentencing for 2 p.m. on the 24th of this month. Lawyer Zou Binghu defended him in court. After that, the court adjourned.

Investigators to Be Sent to Investigate the Case of Trouble Caused by Famine in the Tenth District. The farmers in the tenth district of this county had a conflict with the police team over the famine issue, resulting in the police opening fire and killing three villagers and seriously injuring several others. County Magistrate Tan Yigui immediately telegraphed the provincial government to request punishment. However, the second district party branch of the district sent personnel to conduct a detailed investigation and said, "The trouble was actually caused by the district chief's instructions. The incident location was at Diandang Bridge, more than one li away from the district office. District Chief Wang Hongyu actually ordered the police to open fire and, after the trouble, abandoned the bayonets and guns in the river. Therefore, District Chief Wang is actually guilty of killing innocent civilians without cause." Therefore, they jointly petitioned the Department of Civil Affairs and the provincial government to request that Wang be dismissed from his post, arrested, and punished. It is heard that the provincial government has sent a committee to Changshu to investigate. They are expected to arrive in Changshu within a few days.

Changzhou 81

The Provincial Committee Investigates the Vandalism of the Party Headquarters. After a group of merchants from Wuyi captured a cloth merchant, Hu Ruilin, for being paraded in the streets and placed in a wooden cage, they went to vandalize the county party headquarters and other places and broke open the cage to abduct Hu. Afterwards, the party headquarters urgently telegraphed a report to the provincial party headquarters. The provincial committee has sent Zhou Huapeng to Changzhou on the 19th to investigate the vandalism at the county party headquarters, the Anti-Japanese Association, and the Zhongshan Newspaper Office, and to investigate everything from all sides. In the afternoon, more than 10,000 students and workers gathered at the public sports field and marched in formation to the county government to petition. Zhou Huapeng, a member of the provincial committee, gave a speech expressing the provincial party committee's position that the purpose of punishing the perpetrators must be achieved. Wu Wenbi and Lu Zao, who were injured, were also examined by the county court, and Zhang Chengguan and Ye Jinde, who were involved in the case, were arrested and temporarily taken into custody by the county government. Because the starting point of the case was the Dafengren Cloth Store's opposition to the sealing up of Japanese goods, the store has been sealed up and the public has been informed. The student side has decided to resume classes as usual from the 20th.

Jiangyin 82

Passengers on the Xicheng Bus Demand Compensation for Losses. At about 9 a.m. on the 17th, the Xicheng long-distance bus No. 7 overturned into a ditch near Tangtou Bridge because it was carrying too many passengers. The driver, Gao Afu, was careless. The passengers included Xu Zihou from the Gengyuanyin Silk Shop (Zhong Deli, Beijingli, Shanghai), Hu Yukang from the Juchangxiang Silk Shop (Jingheli, Sanmalu), Jiang Nianchun from the Baohuaxiang Cotton Cloth Shop (Taozhuli, Sanmalu), Zeng Haoren from the Rixinheng Cotton Cloth Shop (Gongguan Road), Lu Qinhou from the Tongfu Cotton Cloth Shop (Donghuali, Simalu), Mao Songting (seriously injured in the hand), Wang Jilin from the Anji Silk Shop (Yonganli, Tianjin Road), and Yao Xuemen from the Yuancang Cotton Cloth Shop (Xiangfennongkou, Damalu) (seriously injured in the head). Most of them came to Cheng to pursue Wan Yusen for compensation for losses of 142 silver dollars in cash, gold rings, silver watches, and other items. Yesterday (the 19th), they sent separate letters to the county chamber of commerce to forward them to the Xicheng Bus Company, requesting full compensation.

Zhenjiang 83

Officials Sent to County to Handle Seed Loans. In order to provide disaster relief to agriculture after the disaster by lending seeds to disaster areas, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture had telegraphed the Ministry of Industry to transfer 1,400 tons of American wheat provided by the National Government's Disaster Relief Committee to the department for lending to ten counties, including Baoying. However, American wheat cannot be used as seed, and the deadline is imminent. Therefore, the committee requested Lu Xiaobo, the chairman of the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, to inform the local grain shops or flour mills to first borrow domestic wheat for application. After the American wheat arrives in Shanghai, it will be returned separately. Meanwhile, the department has assigned ten committee members to go to the county to handle the matter. The department committee members have all departed today.

Jiangpu 84

The Rice Case Between Jiangpu and Liuhe Comes to an End. The rice merchants of Jiangpu and Chu County transported rice through the territory of Chu County to Zhangjiabao on the Chu River, which borders Liuhe. However, due to unmet conditions, the district chief and many others suddenly advocated "striking the border," making it appear to be true. The incident lasted for many days, and more than 300 boats were detained successively, resulting in huge losses for both the rice merchants and the boat owners. The provincial government repeatedly sent two provincial committee members to order the Liuhe industry to release all the boats on the 9th. The case can be said to have come to an end. The telegram from Hu, the Minister of Civil Affairs, in response to County Magistrate Xia, is recorded below, as are the telegrams from Yu and Qi, the two acting telegrams, and the two successive reports. It is known that County Magistrate Hong of Liuhe handled the case improperly. For the time being, he will be given a warning and a demerit. As for the rest, after the Anhui people investigate and find out who opened fire and caused the trouble, the cases will be considered together. The removal and investigation of the chiefs of the fourth and fifth districts have also been clearly ordered. The above are all on file. You should quickly inform the county of this and urge the remaining six grain boats to return to Pu and wait for a legal solution.

Two Japanese Warships Cruise Off the Coast of Dinghai. Yu Kangshu and Others Post Bail in Hangzhou. The case of Yu Kangshu, the captain of the Detective Team of the Ningbo Public Security Bureau, and team member Zhu Fuxing, who were beaten to death due to torture and forced confessions, was improperly handled by the Yinxian District Court Prosecutor's Office. He Jinshi, the wife of the victim, petitioned the High Court to allow the transfer of jurisdiction to the Hangzhou District Court for trial. The court summoned Yu and Zhu to Hangzhou yesterday. Jiaxing 87

The Water Police District Department Asks the County to Raise Public Debt in Cash on Its Behalf. The wages of the water police in the second district of Jiaxing have been in arrears for more than five months. Now, Chief Zhou has requested the province to allocate funds. The province has issued four months' worth, but it has also issued 80% of the old debt public bonds to clear the debts of this province for 20 years, totaling more than 15,000 yuan in face value. Chief Zhou believes that the bonds are difficult to use in the market, so he consulted with the county government to ask the local chambers of commerce and gentry to raise cash on its behalf in order to issue wages to the teams. The county government followed the methods for raising public debt in each district and ordered each district office on the 19th to raise the number of bonds to be paid to the county within five days so that they could be sent to the water police district office for distribution.

Scheduled Meeting to Discuss Important Disaster Preparedness Policies. Jiaxing's autumn harvest this year was greatly reduced, and rice prices cannot be reduced. Rice merchants from various places come to Jiaxing to purchase large quantities of rice for export. It is expected that during the period between the spring and summer harvests, not only will rice prices be high, but there will also be a shortage of grain. Citizens such as Cha Ren of this county telegraphed the province to order the county to form a disaster preparedness organization to prepare funds to purchase rice for storage in case of emergencies. Now, after receiving the telegram from the province, the county government has sent separate letters to local gentry and representatives of various legal organizations to schedule a meeting on the 25th to discuss important disaster preparedness policies to prevent rice shortages.

Xiaoshan 88

Profiteering Merchants Paraded Through the Streets. Qu Youchuan, a profiteering merchant from Yiqiao, Xiaoshan, runs a large general merchandise store there. During the sealing up of Japanese goods, not only did he not register as required, but he also colluded with his peers, Yidadafeng Weikang and Nanhua stores Yuanchun Gongtai Kaitai, etc., to take this opportunity to solicit business and hold a large auction of Japanese goods. The local Anti-Japanese Association went to stop them because the stores did not register according to the law but instead engaged in large auctions. Qu actually cursed loudly. After discussion, it was decided at the meeting yesterday to parade Qu Youchuan through the streets with a white flag of a profiteering merchant. The stores were also punished. Officials Cannot Serve in People's Organizations. This time, the counties organized anti-Japanese activities completely by popular initiative. The provincial government previously received orders from the central government that the people's salvation and anti-Japanese activities were indeed the true will of the people, and government offices must not interfere and cannot serve as committee members in the people's self-organized work. The people of Xiaoshan are quite spirited in their self-organized anti-Japanese activities, but officials serving as committee members are in violation of provincial orders and have completely withdrawn.

Important Educational News

Implementation Principles of the Three People's Principles Education Promulgated by the Ministry of Education (4) 89

Section 2 Implementation Guidelines

(1) Curriculum

Regarding Social Sciences:

1. Should integrate the strengths of Eastern and Western cultures with the spirit of the Three People's Principles.

2. Should connect the entire teachings of Mr. Sun Yat-sen with the teaching materials to establish the social sciences of the Three People's Principles.

3. Should thoroughly study the essence of academic principles in order to create the cultural values of the Three People's Principles.

Regarding Natural Sciences:

1. Should focus on knowledge and skills in production technology.

2. Should conclude research or design with the completion of material construction.

3. Should thoroughly engage in scientific research and devote efforts to inventions that benefit mankind and advance civilization.

Regarding Party Principles Courses:

1. Should focus on elaborating on the entire teachings of Mr. Sun Yat-sen and the party's program, policies, and important declarations.

2. Should demonstrate through theory and facts that the Three People's Principles are the only revolutionary principles for completing the national revolution and promoting world harmony.

3. Should critically compare and analyze other socialist doctrines based on the Three People's Principles.

(2) Moral Education

1. Should establish a revolutionary outlook on life based on the teachings of Mr. Sun Yat-sen.

2. Should rigorously train strong physiques and a spirit of perseverance through military education and sports activities.

3. Should strictly enforce academic examinations and reward creative works to cultivate a thorough spirit of research.

4. Should cultivate a love of nature and admire the virtues of ritual and music to foster a beautiful and robust personality.

5. Should strictly enforce the "Thrift Movement" and correct romantic habits to cultivate a simple and hardworking lifestyle of ordinary people.

6. Should cultivate habits of organization and discipline through student self-government and appropriate guidance.

7. Should guide the implementation of various cooperative enterprises to cultivate a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation.

8. Should encourage and guide the organization of various service groups to penetrate the inner layers of society, engage in improving public knowledge, and reform social advantages and disadvantages to cultivate a spirit of sacrifice and the sense of responsibility that intellectuals should have.

9. Should require all students to participate in the Weekly Memorial Service for the Premier and other revolutionary memorial days to enhance their love for the party and the country.

(3) Equipment

1. The selection of equipment should be based on the principle of realizing the Three People's Principles and not deviating from them.

2. The layout of equipment should be based on the principle of facilitating students' learning and arousing their interest in self-directed research.

3. The content of the equipment should be as comprehensive as possible to provide a basis for the study of advanced academic subjects and should be as open as possible for social observation.

4. Each college or department related to social sciences should establish research rooms for the Three People's Principles, the Five-Power Constitution, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Theory, depending on their nature, in order to establish the social sciences of the Three People's Principles.

5. Each college or department related to natural sciences and applied sciences should establish research rooms for relevant industrial plans, depending on their nature, in order to gradually realize material construction.

6. Laboratories, practice rooms, and other workplaces should be decorated as much as possible with physical objects and charts related to party principles.

7. Should strive to complete the equipment for sports, military training, and related martial arts.

Chapter 4 Normal School Education 90

Section 1 Objectives

1. Should cultivate teachers who can implement the Three People's Principles education by providing the latest scientific education and sound physical and mental training based on the spirit of the Three People's Principles and with reference to the needs of social life.

2. Schools should communicate with society and create an environment that combines "teaching," "learning," and "doing" to enable students to improve the education sector and have a lifelong commitment to service.

3. Rural normal school education should focus on improving rural life and adapting to its needs in order to cultivate talent who can actually engage in rural education or social education.

Section 2 Implementation Guidelines

1. Curriculum

2. The compilation of the curriculum should conform to the years of teacher training and the needs of the local area.

3. Teaching in each subject should pay attention to the application of teaching materials and practice to cultivate students' ability and interest in compiling their own teaching materials.

4. Normal schools should appropriately add courses related to the implementation of social education so that they can also be qualified to be teachers of social education.

5. The rural normal school curriculum should focus on agricultural production and rural improvement teaching materials.

6. The women's normal school curriculum should also emphasize infant care knowledge and home economics practice.

Regulations for Student Teaching in Shandong Province 91

The Ministry of Education, based on the report submitted by the Shandong Provincial Department of Education regarding the regulations for student teaching at Shandong Provincial Normal Schools, has, in accordance with the Ministry's promulgated high school teacher training curriculum standards for practical subjects, revised Articles 2, 3, 4, and 6 together and approved them for record. The Ministry's revised regulations for student teaching in Shandong Province are recorded below:

Article 1 (Omitted)

Article 2: The student teaching period for normal school students is set at three years. Students of provincial normal schools must go to the affiliated and nearby elementary schools of their respective schools for student teaching starting from the first academic year. Students of provincial rural normal schools must do so starting from the second academic year.

Article 3: The order of student teaching for normal school students is as follows:

Phase 1: Observation and discussion of elementary school administration and teaching.

Phase 2: First semester: Observation and discussion of elementary school administration and teaching. Second semester: Observation and discussion of elementary school administration and teaching (with emphasis on observation, but students should still be given scheduled time to observe elementary school administration and teaching).

Phase 3: Practice teaching and discussion of elementary school teaching (with emphasis on practice teaching, but students should still be given scheduled time to observe and observe elementary school administration and teaching).

The duration of each phase of student teaching is one academic year.

Article 4: Phase 1: Observation and discussion should be held at least three times per semester and does not count for academic credit. Phase 2: First semester: Observation for two hours per week (discussion time excluded), counting for two academic credits. Second semester: Observation (with observation attached) for two hours per week (discussion time excluded), counting for two academic credits. Phase 3: Practice teaching (with observation and apprenticeship attached) for five hours per week (discussion time excluded), counting for five academic credits per semester, totaling ten credits.

Article 5: The time and grouping method for normal school students' observation and practice teaching are to be determined by each school independently and reported to the Department of Education for record.

Article 6: Each normal school should organize a student teaching guidance committee to guide students in observation, apprenticeship, practice teaching, and discussion. The guidance methods are to be determined by each school independently and reported to the Department of Education for record.

Article 7: The guidance committee mentioned in the previous article can be divided into two groups: school administration and subject teaching. It should be jointly organized by the school's education faculty, the director of academic affairs, the director of student affairs, the director of administrative affairs, and the faculty and staff of the affiliated elementary school.

Articles 8 and 9 (Omitted)

Annual Meeting to be Held in Zhenjiang on November 14th

Intensifying Anti-Japanese National Salvation Education

Students Studying in Japan Petition in Nanjing for the Second Time 94

Another Twenty Arrived Yesterday

After the first group of students returning from Japan arrived in Shanghai, they sent representatives to Nanjing to petition the Ministry of Education, demanding: (1) Severance of diplomatic relations with Japan; (2) Order the ambassador to lower the flag and return home; (3) Declare war on Japan; (4) Issue travel expenses for students returning from Japan. They returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday because the response from the Ministry of Education was deemed unsatisfactory by the Chinese Students' Association in Japan. Therefore, the association specially dispatched Shi Wuwei and Tian Manyi, two executive committee members, as plenipotentiary representatives to return to the country for a second petition. Yesterday, the two arrived in Shanghai aboard the Japanese ship Takefu Maru. Accompanying them were eighteen others, whose names are as follows: Lin Yaoqing (Railway Vocational School), Huang Qizhi (Senshu University), Lei Zhenfeng (Waseda University Women's Division), Yao Minqian (same as above), Zhou Shiquan (Chuo University), Yang Shichen (Meiji University), Hu Yongsui (same as above), Li Zhiwu (same as above), Jiang Zongming (Industrial University), Zeng Zixia (Waseda University), Gan Gongchen (entered Meiji University), Liu Weibing (same as above), Fang Guo (Tokyo Medical School), Liu Gongpu (Hosei University), Xiong Heng (Military Academy), Wang Jinxiu (Osaka Technical College), Ye Jialie (Meiji University), and Zhou Daru (entered Industrial School). The two representatives, Shi and Tian, ​​took the night express train to Nanjing at 11 PM last night to make a second petition to the Ministry of Education for a satisfactory result and to retain the academic status of returning students, because the supervisors at the embassy in Japan, who issued the boat tickets to returning students, had stated that they would be deprived of their academic status.

Kimie Hitomi's Skills Are Remarkable 101

"Before a Female Athlete Takes the Field" Published - A Must-Read for Chinese Athletes

The "Sports Series" published by the Qinfen Bookstore on Fourth Avenue in Shanghai already has nineteen titles, which are quite popular among sports circles. Kimie Hitomi, a world-renowned female sports prodigy, participated in the World Women's Games twice and set six world track and field records. Her book "Before a Female Athlete Takes the Field" has been translated by Liu Jiaxun and details her personal experience and secrets to victory. It has considerable research on the personality, clothing, hygiene, attitude, etc. of female athletes. The book repeatedly discusses the practice of short-distance running and the long jump. The entire book has over 80,000 words and is attached with photos of female athletes running and long jumping. The printing is excellent, and the cover is beautiful and valuable. Both male and female athletes should benefit greatly from reading it. For the sake of popularization, each book is sold for only 90 cents, with a special 10% discount. An additional fee is required for books purchased by mail order.

Among them, the French government purchased and collected the "Snow in Luxembourg" in the National Art Museum. The art critics commented that Xu Beihong should be regarded as the master of the Chinese Renaissance. Xu Beihong must encourage himself. This is about the process of the production.

3. Regarding the promotion of Chinese art:

Upon receiving the order, Xu Beihong came to Europe to uphold the intentions of the government. Receiving the encouragement from all parties, he made extra efforts to promote Chinese art. In recent years, as Europeans' understanding of Chinese art has increased, he did not want to boast about trivial matters. Therefore, he planned to do a larger-scale project, which could not only represent the greatness of Chinese art but also open up new records of international exchanges. When Xu Beihong first came to Europe, his design for this matter was divided into two steps. The first step was to collect modern Chinese paintings for exhibition in Europe. The second step was to sign agreements with European countries for exchange exhibitions to make it a long-term project. Xu Beihong emphasized modern works because there was a reason. Foreigners are already familiar with the value of Chinese ancient art. When discussing Oriental art, they must regard China as a giant. This has long been a conclusion. In recent years, the Japanese government has taken advantage of China's troubles and misappropriated huge sums of money to vigorously promote Japanese modern art, pretending to be the only highest position in the East. Even Europeans generally regard China as the past and only know Japan but do not know China. Xu Beihong saw this and thought about how to make up for it, so he decided on the above plan. When Xu Beihong lived in Paris, he exchanged opinions on art with more than a dozen masters such as A. Besnard, Aman-Jean, Van Dongen, Maurice Doenis, and Landeski, and art administrators such as Paul Leon and A. Deaarroi. Xu Beihong immediately proposed holding a Chinese modern painting exhibition in France first. He immediately collected domestic works to prepare. Then, he made an agreement with the director of the National Art Museum, Mr. Deaarroi, to hold it in Paris in the winter of 1933.
