Li Jishen, Yu Youren and Other Guangdong Representatives Arrive in Shanghai; Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Others Will Arrive This Morning 103

Li Jishen, Yu Youren and Others Arrive in Shanghai 104

Each Committee Member States That There is No Such Thing as a Conference

Only Committee Members From Nanjing and Guangdong Will Meet to Discuss National Affairs

Former Chairman of the Guangdong Political Council, Li Jishen and his wife, President of the National Government's Control Yuan, Yu Youren, and Central Committee members Wu Tiecheng, Shao Yuanchong, Li Shizeng, Zhu Peide, and Zhou Qigang, due to the imminent arrival of Guangdong representatives Wang Jingwei and others in Shanghai, arrived here at around 8:00 AM yesterday. In addition to dispatching military police to provide strict protection, the Shanghai Garrison Command, Public Security Bureau, and authorities from both sides also dispatched Chen Mingshu, Commander-in-Chief of the 19th Route Army, and others to welcome them at the North Railway Station.

Conditions at the Station: Li Jishen and other Central Committee members traveled in three first-class sleeper cars. Li and his wife and son rode in rooms 105 and 106. He was wearing an orange serge long gown. He looked quite plump. In the car, he read newspapers and chatted with friends in a very calm manner. After arriving at the station at 8:05 AM, the committee members got off the train one after another. Li and his wife and others were the last to come out. He shook hands with Chen Mingshu and others, then went out and rode in Chen's car with his young son to rest in a private residence in the French Concession. His wife and other committee members also took cars to their respective residences to rest.

Li Jishen's Speech: Yesterday, Li Jishen told this newspaper's reporter that he came here to meet with the Central Committee members in Guangdong, whom he had not seen for a long time. He had no specific proposals for the peace conference. He firmly believed that with the national crisis at hand, party comrades would definitely unite sincerely and resist foreign aggression. Therefore, the future of the peace conference was extremely optimistic. When asked whether members of the first, second, and third Central Committees would attend the meeting, he said that he had not heard anything about it in Nanjing. This newspaper's reporter also asked Chen Mingshu about the date when the 19th Route Army would open its defense in Shanghai. He said that because of the lack of ships recently, it would take some time to reach Shanghai.

Wu Tiecheng's Speech: According to the New Voice News Agency, Wu Tiecheng said that there was no such thing as a preparatory meeting or a formal meeting for the peace conference. Rather than calling it a preparatory meeting or a formal meeting, it would be better to call it a meeting between the committee members from Nanjing and Guangdong to discuss national affairs. Whether a meeting would be held to discuss matters tonight (i.e., last night) after the Guangdong representatives arrived in Shanghai would depend on the time of Wang's arrival. He had seen the opinions put forward by Li Liejun and others on the peace conference, and he thought there was no problem with them. It was still unclear whether Li Liejun, Cheng Qian, Xu Qian, and others would be invited to participate in the future meeting.

Zhu and Shao's Speech: According to the New Voice News Agency, Committee Members Zhu Peide and Shao Lizi said that they came here to meet with the committee members and there was no so-called peace preparatory meeting. Since they were meeting for the country's sake, they took the opportunity to discuss matters and then invited them to Nanjing to discuss national affairs together. Furthermore, it was not yet certain whether Chiang would come to Shanghai, but he would probably arrive today or tomorrow.

Yu and Li's Speech: The New Voice News Agency interviewed Yu Youren in the car, and Committee Member Li Shizeng was also inside. The reporter asked for their opinions on the peace conference and the Japanese atrocities. Both of them were unwilling to make any comments, but said that they came to Shanghai not to participate in any conference, and there was no such thing as a formal meeting or a preparatory meeting. They were only meeting with the committee members for a discussion.

Zhou Qigang's Speech: The progress of the peace movement is considerable, and the future is extremely optimistic. After the committee members meet each other, they will definitely put aside all differences and jointly formulate plans for national affairs and unanimously resist foreign aggression. After Wang and others arrive in Shanghai, the two sides will have a discussion, and then the committee members will be invited to Nanjing. As for the date and location of the peace conference and how it will be convened, he had not heard anything about it and it seemed that it had not yet been decided. According to his personal observation, in this consultation, the point of uniting the Nanjing and Guangdong sides seems to be easily resolved. The central government has no preconceptions. The Guangdong committee members will still return to Nanjing to jointly take responsibility for the party and the country and unite to resist foreign invasion. The central government has already restored the party membership of all comrades who were expelled from the party due to political reasons. It is not difficult to resolve previous misunderstandings, so unity is not a problem. If such internal rectification can be avoided, it would be better to resolve it by means of a meeting. Otherwise, it can be easily resolved after the committee members discuss it. Chairman Chiang may come to Shanghai in the next few days to meet with the Guangdong committee members.

Late-Night Talk Among Central Committee Members

Explaining the Opinions of the Nanjing Committee Members

Discussing the Location of the Meeting Today or Tomorrow

Yesterday's Discussion: After the Central Committee members from Nanjing arrived in Shanghai yesterday, with the exception of Li Renchao, eight members including Yu Youren, Zhang Jingjiang, Wu Tiecheng, Li Shizeng, Shao Yuanchong, Shao Lizi, Zhu Peide, and Chen Mingshu, agreed to go to the new residence of Hu Hanmin on Maierxi Ai Road at 5:00 PM to hold a discussion. In addition to the above eight committee members, Liu Luyin also participated. The committee members discussed for about one and a half hours, and left at 6:25 PM. According to the New Voice News Agency, in addition to explaining the opinions of the Nanjing committee members to Hu and others, the meeting also discussed the location of the meeting. It is expected that after the Guangdong representatives arrive in Shanghai today, they will first exchange views at Sun's residence or Hu's residence, in preparation for opening the preparatory meeting. As for the location of the preparatory meeting, it has not yet been determined.

Guangdong Representatives Will Arrive This Morning 105

Originally Scheduled to Arrive in Shanghai Last Night, But Delayed Due to Wind

The representatives sent by Guangdong to attend the peace conference, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Wu Chaoshu, Li Wenfan, Lin Sen, Chen Youren, and others, were traveling on the President Madison, a liner from the Dollar Steamship Company. They were originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 7:30 PM last night. All parties were prepared to go to the Pudong wharf to welcome them on time. However, yesterday afternoon, the Dollar Steamship Company and Chen Mingshu and others received a radio report from the liner stating that the ship would have to be delayed until 8:30 AM today (the 21st) due to wind. The welcomers temporarily suspended their departure and will go to the wharf again this morning to meet them. The company will depart from the Xinguang Wharf at 8:30 AM this morning with a small steamship to carry passengers and welcomers. Furthermore, the Special District Citizens' Federation specially dispatched representatives yesterday to welcome Mr. Wang Jingwei with a letter this morning. The letter said: "Reverently, the violent Japanese are wreaking havoc, sending troops to invade the west. The mountains and rivers of the two provinces of Liaoning and Jilin have changed color, and the sound of alarms can be heard frequently. The foundation of the country is shaking. At this moment, to resist foreign aggression, we must first quell internal disputes, which has become the common wish of the people. Our federation previously sent representative Wang Hanliang to Guangdong to petition, which we hope has been taken into consideration. Fortunately, you have upheld the late Premier's legacy of peace and national salvation, and comforted the people's pain of hoping for good governance. You are willing to come and work together. We will see peace and unity, lay the foundation of our country, and work together to eliminate the Japanese pirates. Our federation intends to respectfully welcome you on the day of your arrival and will publicly elect representatives Wang Hanliang, Yu Hualong, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, and Jiang Xinzhao, with more than a hundred representatives from the subordinate branches, to stand and welcome you, to show the Shanghai people's yearning for peace. Our humble sincerity, we hope you will accept with favor."

Hu Hanmin's Actions Yesterday 106

Hu Says Steps Will Be Determined After Guangdong Representatives Arrive

Sun Yat-sen's Spirit of Universal Love Is Not a Tool for Struggle

After Hu Hanmin moved to 301 Mai'erxi Road, yesterday (the 20th), people from all walks of life continued to visit him in an endless stream. In the morning, groups such as representatives from the dockworkers' union organizing committee, the Chinese Students' Association in Japan, and the Shanghai university anti-Japanese salvation associations, totaling more than 30 people, arrived. Individuals who visited included Li Jishen, Shao Yuanchong, Chen Fumu, Feng Ziyou, and others. Li Jishen and Hu Hanmin had a teacher-student relationship and had not seen each other for more than two years, so their conversation was quite lively, lasting from 10 a.m. to 12 p.m., a total of two hours. After the conversation, they took a group photo to commemorate the occasion before Li bid farewell and left. Subsequently, Wu Tiecheng visited Hu and talked for about an hour. In the afternoon, representatives from the Chinese Nationalist Party's Protection of the Party Comrades Association, representatives of the Jilin people, representatives of the Shanghai publishing industry workers' union, and Zhou Peizhen, Zhang Weichen, and others visited Hu and briefly conversed before departing. As of yesterday, Hu Hanmin had received telegrams of condolences from more than 130 groups. The Honolulu General Branch of the Nationalist Party also telegraphed, recommending Cheng Runquan, a representative to the Fourth National Congress, to convey their condolences to Hu.

Hu Hanmin's Conversation with a News Agency Reporter. Yesterday, after Hu met with his guests, a reporter from the News Agency paid a visit to Hu Hanmin and asked for his views on the prospects of peaceful reunification. According to Hu, the entire process of peaceful reunification must wait until the Guangdong delegates arrive in Shanghai to exchange views before determining the next steps. There is currently no such thing as a preparatory meeting or a formal meeting. As for peaceful reunification, it is something that everyone urgently hopes for, but the outcome depends on whether everyone can truly abandon their personal interests and deeply recognize that the Party and the country are paramount. Most importantly, everyone must be able to acknowledge their past mistakes and correct future ones. However, after peaceful reunification, there must be political reforms, diplomatic reforms, and all measures must be well reformed before it can be called true peaceful reunification, otherwise the result will still be zero. He then said that any proposals from all parties, if they are considered in the interest of the Party and the country, can be submitted sooner or later. In short, Sun Yat-sen's spirit of universal love should not be used as a tool for personal struggle.

Hu's Conversation with Students. At 9 a.m. yesterday, the Chinese Students' Association in Japan sent Yi Zhichao and Shen Zairen as representatives to visit Hu Hanmin. After the meeting, the representatives reported on the recent high-pressure tactics of the Japanese government against overseas Chinese in the academic, business, and industrial sectors, as well as the past work of the delegation and future directions. At the same time, they requested guidance. Hu gave detailed instructions on each point. Regarding the work, it is best to divide the work and cooperate, and it is important to pay attention to publicity. If publicity is limited to shouting slogans such as "Boycott Japanese goods" and "Down with imperialism," it will lose its effectiveness. It is necessary to expose the consistent ambition of Japan and Korea to annex our Northeast China in order to arouse the attention of our compatriots at home and abroad. Secondly, when asked about the delegation's request to the Ministry of Education for funds to cover the travel expenses of all those returning to China, Representative Xiang gave a detailed account of the Ministry of Education's difficulty in approving the request. Mr. Hu expressed great sympathy for the request of all students in Japan to return to China, and immediately instructed a certain member of the Central Committee to ask the National Government to provide travel expenses for the students in Japan to return to China.

Li Yue Arrives in Shanghai. Li Yue, the brigade commander of the Fourth Front Army of Guangdong, was at the forefront of the anti-communists. After the loss of Liaoning and Jilin, he traveled alone to various provinces along the Yangtze River to appeal for peace. When he arrived in southern Jiangxi, he was intercepted by the communists for several days and nearly met with disaster. He has now escaped danger. Hearing that Mr. Hu Hanmin had arrived in Shanghai and that Wang Jingwei and Sun Ke were also coming, he took a flight to Shanghai yesterday and plans to visit Hu today and report to Wang and Sun.

Declaration of the Shanghai Guangdong People's United National Salvation Association 107

Declaration of the Shanghai Guangdong People's United National Salvation Association to Promote the Ning-Yue Peace Conference: Respected Ning-Yue ruling officials and compatriots across the country, since the Japanese army's riot in Northeast China on September 18, they have invaded cities, seized land, and killed countless people. Their fierce flames are high and progressing with the times. That violent Japan is not satisfied with swallowing the Northeast and has even created the absurd theory of the complete independence of Manchuria and Mongolia. Their malicious intentions are completely exposed. At this time of national crisis, if we across the country cannot unite sincerely and resist Japan, it will not only allow the brigands to run rampant without fear, but also allow them to enter our homes and completely reduce the Northeast border and the entire Central Plains to the second Korea or the second India. The arrival of foreign aggression originates from self-humiliation. The decline of the Qing Dynasty was due to the昏庸 (hunyong - muddle-headedness and incompetence) of the court, the weakness after the founding of the Republic of China was due to the tyranny of the Northern Warlords, and the lack of progress after the Northern Expedition was due to the division of the Nationalist Party. Therefore, the way to save the country and strengthen it is to first focus on self-strengthening. The so-called human justice and international public reason are all delusional dreams and the pretexts of thieves. This is further confirmed by the hypocritical attitude of the League of Nations after the Northeast Incident. Therefore, from now on, we must only use iron against iron, blood against blood, and unite the strength of the entire country to fight to the death with violent Japan. Fortunately, the Ning-Yue ruling officials, in this time of crisis, saw righteousness and acted bravely, resolved old grievances, and sincerely sought peace and cooperation to plan a united front against foreign aggression. Now that representatives from both sides are about to gather in Shanghai to discuss national affairs, we hope that the ruling officials will earnestly consult and decide on national policies, and rescue our people from the abyss of suffering and place our national foundation on a rock. We also hope that our compatriots across the country will work together to demand and urge that the Ning-Yue peace and unity against Japan be realized. We, as members of the nation, have an inescapable responsibility. Therefore, we unite the townships and clans of the city, unify our will and pace, and vow to be the vanguard of resisting Japan and saving the country, and to be the backing for the peace and unity conference. We hereby declare.

Anti-Japanese National Salvation Movement 108

Emergency Notice from the Anti-Japanese Association Yesterday

Confiscated Non-Japanese Goods Can Be Claimed for Return

Please Citizens Do Not Purchase Goods from Xie Da Xiang

Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Executive Committee Announcement No. 11: It is noted that the former Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee issued the 7th announcement, item 3 of the measures for dealing with Japanese goods, "After July 24, those who purchase or transport Japanese goods (industrial raw materials are excluded because there are other measures) will have them confiscated." According to confidential reports, the Xie Da Xiang Tongji foreign cloth store in Xiaodongmen violated the announcement and privately imported Japanese goods and sold them in large quantities. On the 17th of this month, the Association sent personnel to inspect the store. The store obstructed in every possible way and even dared to report to the police, detaining the three inspectors for interrogation. This was a deliberate attempt to undermine the anti-Japanese movement and to promote the sale of Japanese goods. After detailed discussion by the 8th Executive Committee of the Association, it was unanimously agreed that (1) all the Japanese goods in the store should be confiscated; (2) the manager should be handed over to the Disciplinary Committee for punishment; (3) the banking industry should be informed not to provide loans to the store. In addition to the separate implementation of these measures by the Association, all citizens of the city should be notified not to purchase goods from Xie Da Xiang in the future to show their determination. Otherwise, the Association will not be responsible for any goods purchased from the store that are found on the way. Please pay close attention.

Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Executive Committee Announcement No. 12: For the purpose of notification, the Association has now formulated a form for investigating claims for confiscated goods for the convenience of investigation. Any owner of confiscated goods who believes that the goods are not Japanese and requests their return may bring proof and relevant documents to the secretariat of the Association at Tianhou Temple to obtain the claim form, fill it out according to the instructions, and submit it to the Association for verification. Other letters that do not follow this procedure will not be accepted. For fear of not being fully informed, this announcement is made.

Visit Hu, Request Restoration of Sino-Russian Relations

Oppose Direct Sino-Japanese Negotiations

Hu Tigan, Jiang Shoushan, Che Xiangchen, Liu Shilin, Yang Yuxiu, and Liu Mengpo, representatives of the people of Northeast China, have now arrived in Shanghai and were received by the Municipal Party Department, which promised to assist in contacting various schools to report on the Northeast Incident next Monday during the memorial week. Anti-Japanese Resistance in Shipping News 111

Chinese Employees of Japanese Ships Resign. All foreign merchant ships traveling on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River must use Chinese pilots. Since the anti-Japanese national salvation movement began, Chinese pilots on Japanese merchant ships from Hankou upwards, through Yichang and Wanxian to Chongqing, have automatically submitted their resignations to the Japanese shipping companies out of patriotic indignation. Since the 16th of this month, the Japanese ships in the upper reaches have been unable to travel due to the lack of pilots. In addition, the Chinese workers on the Japanese ship Changfeng Maru, which travels on the Sichuan River, have all resigned and left the ship. This ship has also been stopped.

Workers Refuse to Unload Japanese Goods. The Osaka Company's Sherpis Maru arrived in Shanghai from Southeast Asia, carrying 1,000 tons of rice from Siam and other places, to be unloaded at the Yitai Hing Wharf. Driven by patriotism, the workers at the wharf refused to unload the Japanese ship's cargo. Another Japanese ship was also treated in the same way. Later, the Japanese spent a large amount of money to change the ships and unload the goods.

Japanese Ships No Longer Go to Xiamen. The Osaka Company has many ships on the Xiamen, Shantou, Guangdong, and Taiwan routes. After a unified boycott by the industrial and commercial sectors, it telegraphed to order all ships to abandon the port of Xiamen. At the same time, the Japanese in Xiamen colluded with the Taiwanese to stir up trouble in every possible way. The Japanese warship Take in Xiamen has taken the opportunity to dispatch marines ashore under the pretext of 調陸戰隊上岸 (tiaoluzhandui shang'an - deploying marines ashore).

More Students Returning from Japan. More students returning from Japan include Yu Shunmin, Yang Jinxi, Lin Xiru, Li Huimin, Yi Xiangying, Yu Zhongyao, Wei Wukuan, Zhou Daru, Tian Zaojia, Yang Shizhu, Wang Jinxiu, and 41 others, who arrived in Shanghai from Tokyo, Kobe, and other places. More are expected to arrive in the next few days.

Large Numbers of Overseas Chinese Returning to China. In recent days, more than 2,000 overseas Chinese have returned to China from Japan. In the past two days, more have arrived in Shanghai on the Chichibu Maru from Tokyo, including Wang Shanchu, Lin Rongkai, and 147 others; on the Shanghai Maru, including Yang Zhaozuo, Zhuang Zhaoxiang, and 238 others; on the Mikasa Maru, including Feng Deyuan and 80 others; on the Tsukuba Maru, including Zhao Dengkui and 46 others; on the Maya Maru, including Ding Fangdian and 60 others. In these two days, a total of 525 people have arrived.

Anti-Japanese Activities in All Circles 112

Inspection Work of the First District Branch of the Municipal Association. Yesterday morning at 9 a.m., the First District Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Federation convened more than 30 people, including all members of the Japanese Goods Inspection Committee and professionals from various industries, and divided them into groups and industries. (Group A) Silk, wool, foreign goods, and cotton weaving industries: inspectors He Guangsheng, Xu Meiqing, Hu Lifu, Zhou Guansong, Yuan Chuanhua, Weng Zhilian, Wu Chuansheng, Li Hede; (Group B) Cosmetics, foreign sundries, pharmacies, photography, and Chinese medicine industries: inspectors Sun Wenyi, Tang Chengzhang, Pan Ruitang, Tang Yutian, Sun Yuxiang, Lu Jinghua; (Group C) Southern goods, wine, vegetables, porcelain, and canned food industries: inspectors Le Fucheng, Yu Yanting, Le Rucheng, Chen Jusheng, Cai Hanzhang, Zhang Lieming, Zhang Songling; (Group D) Electrical appliances, clocks, watches, eyeglasses, stationery, paper, and gramophone industries: inspectors Li Jianliang, Zhuang Zhihe, Chen Duomin, Tao Zhiqian, Bei Shijun, Wu Guorui, Xiang Kejia; (Group E) Tobacco, paper, hardware, jewelry, and other industries: inspectors Wang Lianfang, Fei Xingzhuang, Chen Siyu. They departed at the same time and inspected each household and industry in the Nanjing Road area of the Association, respectively. The members expressed goodwill during the inspection. Most of the stores that had already been sealed up had no Japanese goods left. A small number of stores that had not been sealed up immediately sorted out the Japanese goods on the spot and had them sealed up by the inspectors. Finally, they were affixed with a "Inspected" label. The inspection was completed at 6 p.m. It was decided that from today onwards, a member on duty will be stationed at the Association to wait for members from the General Association to accompany them for re-inspection.

The Municipal Association Begins to Inspect Japanese Goods. The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Association regards the inspection of Japanese goods as the first step in implementing economic severance, and its duties are not to be delayed. A Japanese Goods Inspection Team has been organized and has begun to inspect stores on various roads. Yesterday, team members Wang Zhaocheng, Liu Zhongying, Wu Banjiang, Wang Qingping, Jiang Xianhe, Xu Yunhui, Lin Yangzhi, Ye Qichang, Zhang Henghai, Shi Jiulin, and others were appointed to begin inspecting stores in the Nanjing Road area today.

Telegram to Honolulu Overseas Chinese Urging Persistence in Boycotting Goods. Cheng Runquan, representative from Honolulu, telegraphed to all overseas Chinese in Honolulu yesterday, "Honolulu Chinese Public Report to all comrades and overseas Chinese, violent Japan has sent troops to occupy Northeast China, the whole country is grief-stricken, in addition to vigorously calling for great unity at home, we earnestly urge you to persist in boycotting Japanese goods, the survival of life and death is at stake, Cheng Runquan."

Meeting Minutes of the Pearl and Jade Industry Association. The Pearl and Jade Industry Association held an emergency meeting of representatives at 3 p.m. on the 18th at the Association at 25 Houjia Road to discuss anti-Japanese national salvation and other cases. The meeting was held as scheduled, and Zhang Wendi, Zhang Bingxin, and Lian Zixiang were elected as the temporary presidium. Two major proposals were reported: (1) Effective anti-Japanese national salvation implementation plan. (A) Abiding by the municipal government's transfer of the National Government's support of the telegram, the country is in dire straits, domestic discipline and order must be maintained at any cost. Decision: Unanimously respect the whole people's foreign affairs. (B) Fundraising for the anti-Japanese national salvation association's operating expenses. Decision: Hold a special donation campaign for members and do our best to raise funds. (C) Approval of the city Chamber of Commerce's transfer, the Anti-Japanese Association's approval, and Mr. Yi Huaizeng's proposal that each store must add a stamp to the invoice certifying that it is not Japanese goods. Decision: Notify member stores to strictly follow. (D) Implementation of Japanese goods inspection. Decision: This industry has always regarded Japanese cultured pearls as counterfeits and has strictly prohibited them for a long time, never relaxing slightly. Therefore, since the establishment of the inspection team, no Japanese goods have been found. From now on, implement the resolutions of the Japanese Goods Inspection Committee, implement inspection, and work hard. (E) The Municipal Anti-Japanese Association's letter, economic severance, item 3, assigns responsibility to each industry not to supply raw materials to the Japanese. Decision: Proceed in unison. (F) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's letter, transferring the letter from the Great China Match Company, etc., requesting the promotion of domestic goods. Decision: Do our best to adopt them. (G) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce's letter, transferring the letter from Standing Committee Member Xu Jiting, with the practical plan for boycotting Japanese goods drafted by Mr. Zhongxia, which has been published in the Shen and Min newspapers. Decision: Refer to it as much as possible. Member representative Zhu Baoqing proposed that severe penalties should be imposed for inspecting and certifying whether goods are Japanese or not, and that slogans should be printed and posted, etc. Ni Jietang proposed that publicity work should be strengthened. Passed and handed over to the Executive Committee and Inspection Team to plan and implement in earnest. Finally, the second case, the municipal business tax, was reported that the Association had petitioned the municipal government and the Jingyuan Ministry to follow the example of the gold and silver jewelry industry and collect it according to the capital amount.

The Anti-Japanese Branch of Students in Japan Relocates. After the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Students' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association was established, registration was immediately carried out with great enthusiasm and submitted to the Municipal Government and the Municipal Party Department for filing. The Chinese Ratepayers Association Again Asks to Stop Japanese Riots 114

Please Pay Attention to What Judge Feetham Said about the Rule of Law. The Shanghai Municipal Council Met with the Japanese Side Yesterday.

Indicates that it does not favor any party

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association, in view of the reported Japanese riots and the reports from ratepayers Yang Cheng, Feng Yi, etc., sent another letter yesterday to Mr. Macnaghten, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, "Dear Sir, on October 2, we wrote to your Bureau requesting that it stop the Japanese Marines from freely landing to demonstrate. However, Japan does not regard the League of Nations as an organization that should be respected, and even less does it regard your Bureau as an agency that can be respected. This is why the Japanese Marines continue to land at will and run rampant everywhere, and the Japanese residents incite crowds to carry out disturbances to disrupt public order. However, from your Bureau's point of view, you should value the security and rule of law mentioned by Judge Feetham and use the entire police force to maintain peace and order. If your Bureau tolerates the Japanese residents inciting crowds to run rampant and the Japanese Marines freely landing without seeking effective ways to fundamentally stop them, then your Bureau is showing people a division and weakness of the police force, which will make the residents of the Concession only consider ways to protect themselves in a legitimate manner and assist your Bureau in stopping the Japanese military and civilians from running rampant in the Concession. Regarding the security and rule of law in the Concession, we hereby write to your Bureau to clearly indicate whether it can effectively stop the division of the police force, so as to consider whether to seek other positive and effective methods to maintain peace and order.

According to the "Great Beauty Evening News," this morning (the 20th), Mr. Macnaghten, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Mr. Murai, the Japanese Consul-General, and Mr. Fukushima and Okamoto, Japanese directors, the commander of the Japanese landing marines, and Mr. Fessenden, Secretary-General of the Municipal Council, and Chief of Police Martin, held an important meeting in the Municipal Council, which lasted until after noon. It is reported that the meeting was at the request of the Japanese authorities and received the full support of the Concession authorities, as both sides were eager to cooperate with each other to maintain security and order in the Public Concession. During the meeting, the Japanese side stated that the purpose of the Marines' landing was purely to protect the lives and property of Japanese residents and had no other intentions. The Municipal Council also said that it welcomed full cooperation, but stated that it had to strictly maintain neutrality in its efforts to maintain order and could not favor any party. The Municipal Council and the Japanese authorities are currently discussing ways for the Japanese Marines and the police to cooperate as much as possible to maintain security.

Investigation Result of Population in the French Concession 115

Totaling 456,012 People

The results of the population survey in the French Concession were released yesterday. The Chinese and foreign residents have greatly increased over the past year, with a total population of 456,012. This is an increase of 11,105 people compared to the 434,807 found in the same period last year. Chinese residents account for 440,866, an increase of 8,881, while foreigners account for 15,146, an increase of 2,224. The large increase in the number of foreigners is unprecedented in the French Concession. In the previous two years, the number of foreigners increased by only 1,545. This year's sudden increase of over 2,000 is indeed noteworthy. Currently, Russians account for the largest number of foreigners, reaching 5,671, followed by the British at 2,625, and then Americans at 1,572. The French are only in fourth place at 1,326. There are also 581 Germans, 450 residents of Tokyo, 318 Japanese, 303 Portuguese, 262 Poles, 181 Danes, 131 Italians, 105 Dutch. Other nationalities all number less than one hundred, such as 94 Swiss, 87 Spanish, 71 Armenians, 74 Greeks, 63 Norwegians, 63 Belgians, 62 Latvians, 60 Czechs, 48 Romanians, 46 Swedes, 42 Estonians, 36 Austrians, 36 Lithuanians, 28 Syrians, 22 Hungarians, 19 Finns, 16 Yugoslavians, 10 Persians, 9 Brazilians, 7 Turks, 6 Egyptians, 5 Argentinians, 4 Georgians, 3 Mexicans, 3 residents of Santo Domingo, 3 Chileans, 2 Peruvians, and 1 each from Bulgaria, Uruguay, Serbia, and Cuba. Looking at the gender breakdown, among Chinese residents, there are 173,017 males over 15 years old, 64,411 males under 15 years old, 107,353 females over 15 years old, and 45,996 females under 15 years old. Among foreigners, there are 6,447 males over 15 years old, 2,228 males under 15 years old, 4,253 females over 15 years old, and 1,459 females under 15 years old. In addition, there are 19,381 non-residents and 23,055 residents who were temporarily away during the survey.

It is also noted that the total population in 1900 was only 92,268, in 1910 it was still only 115,946, in 1920 it increased to 170,229, in 1925 it increased to 297,092, and in 1930 it increased to 434,807.

Hou Dachun and the Overseas Chinese Aid Donation Case 117

Hou Dachun, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, previously served as a standing committee member and director of the Inspection Section of the All-Circles Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Committee. He solicited 500 yuan from Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, in the name of the committee. Because the committee has been reorganized into the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, all previous income and expenditure accounts have been closed and reported. Recently, Feng Yixian, the secretary of the association, discovered the matter and reported it to the Central Party Headquarters on October 12. The original report is recorded as follows:

Report for Prosecution: Hou Dachun is accused of fraudulently obtaining money in the name of the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid, embezzling donations for overseas Chinese aid, and is being prosecuted according to law in order to demonstrate national law and party discipline as a warning. Since the Wanxian Massacre occurred, the whole country has been filled with grief and indignation. All circles in this city have organized the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Committee. Hou Dachun, with the qualifications of an alternate executive committee member of the Municipal Party Department, was designated by the Municipal Executive Committee to participate and was elected as a standing committee member and director of the Inspection Section. He was entrusted with the party's mission to lead the patriotic movement, and should have been self-disciplined, striving, and dedicated to fulfill his duties and repay the party and the country. However, Hou Dachun, losing his mind and going to extremes, fraudulently solicited 500 yuan from Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, in the name of the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Committee. On July 24, he sent Wang Yongliang, a staff member of the Inspection Section, to the Commercial Press to affix a seal and collect the money. More than two months have passed, and the name of the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid has been cancelled and reorganized. All donations received from various parties for overseas Chinese aid have also been publicly announced and closed by the Economic Committee. However, the income and expenditure accounts of the Inspection Section have been closed and reported as of the end of September. After searching all income items, there is no item for a donation of 500 yuan from the Commercial Press. According to the previous donations to the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Committee, receipts were issued at any time, and stubs were filled in, but there is no record of this payment, which can be verified. It is clear that Hou Dachun fraudulently obtained money in the name of fraud, embezzled patriotic donations, deliberately concealed the matter, only cared about his own illegal interests, willingly degraded his personality, broke his promises, regarded party discipline as a mere formality, and national law as insignificant. This is indeed undeniable. Such a large amount of donation is not easily forgotten in miscellaneous accounts, and the omission cannot be remedied by fabricated accounts after the report is made, in the hope of escaping punishment. Based on his status and his actions, he has violated the crimes of embezzlement under Articles 356 and 357 of the Criminal Law, as well as the crimes of fraud and breach of trust under Articles 363 and 366 of the same law. Furthermore, he has violated Articles 1 and 4 of the Regulations on the Crime of Violating Oaths by Party Members, as well as the crimes under Article 1, Section 3 and 5 of the Temporary Law on Increased Penalties for Crimes Committed by Party Members. According to Article 69 of the Criminal Law and the interpretation of the Supreme Court's ruling No. 102 of the second year, Hou Dachun should be sentenced concurrently with an increased penalty. Since the term of imprisonment exceeds the period of imprisonment, he should be permanently expelled from the party according to party discipline. In accordance with Article 6 of the Regulations on the Crime of Violating Oaths by Party Members, evidence has been collected and reported, and in accordance with Article 9 of the procedures for punishing party members and party departments, the matter is hereby presented to your esteemed association for thorough investigation and prompt transfer to the court for detention and trial, in order to uphold the party's prestige and serve as a warning. With utmost respect, this report is respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee. Reporter: Feng Yixian, Executive Committee Member of the Sixth District Party Department, currently serving as Executive Committee Member and Deputy Director of the Secretariat of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, and former Secretary of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Committee.

Evidence: Photographs (omitted) (A) Payment voucher from the Commercial Press, (B) Final settlement of the Inspection Section, (C) Employee receipt of the Inspection Section, (D) First announcement of the Economic Committee, (E) Second announcement of the Economic Committee.

Explanation of Evidence: (A) On July 24, the Commercial Press paid the money, and Wang Yongliang, a staff member of the Inspection Section, affixed his personal seal. (B) The Inspection Section was reorganized into the Inspection and Investigation Sections in early September. This is a total settlement of the 7th, 8th, and 9th months, with a total of eight receipts, all of which can be verified by receipts, but there is no Commercial Press donation listed. (C) Wang Yongliang is a staff member of the Inspection Section, and this is a receipt for living expenses. (D) The first announcement of the Economic Committee does not include the Commercial Press donation (already published in this newspaper). (E) The second final announcement of the Economic Committee also does not include the Commercial Press donation (already published in this newspaper).

Report from the First District Party Department: Requesting severe punishment of illegal acts to uphold party discipline. When the Korean Massacre occurred, all circles in this city organized the Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Association. Anyone with a conscience should have done their best to fulfill their responsibilities and enlighten their conscience in order to seek relief. Hou Dachun, the current standing committee member of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, previously served as a standing committee member and director of the Inspection Section of the All-Circles Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Association. In the name of the All-Circles Anti-Japanese Overseas Chinese Aid Association, he received 500 yuan from Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, and sent Wang Yongliang, a staff member of the Inspection Section, to affix a seal and collect the money. The facts are all there, and the evidence is solid. However, when the association was dissolved and reorganized into the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, the Economic Committee published all the relief funds received during the period in Shen Bao and Xin Bao on August 20 and September 20 and declared the end of the association. The Commercial Press's donation of 500 yuan was not mentioned in either of the two announcements. It is undoubtedly the case that Hou Dachun, the person in charge of soliciting donations, swallowed the money. As a party member, he did not know how to keep himself clean and betrayed the public trust by filling his own pockets with public funds for overseas Chinese aid. This is extremely illegal. Therefore, we are specially submitting a report to your esteemed association for verification, requesting that he be immediately expelled from the party and dismissed from his post for severe punishment in order to warn others and protect the party's reputation. This would be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee.

Report from the Fifth District Party Department: The Fifth District Party Department's document on Hou Dachun's malpractice requests a thorough investigation in order to uphold party discipline and maintain the party's prestige. Your esteemed association has a party member, Hou Dachun, who is currently a standing committee member of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, an alternate executive committee member of your association, and a former executive committee member of the Commercial Press Trade Union. In the past, he has worked hard for the workers' movement and party affairs and has been loved by his comrades. Therefore, he has served two terms as an alternate committee member of the Municipal Party Department and a representative of the Shanghai industrial circles at the National Assembly. He has now been elected as Shanghai's representative to the Fourth National Congress of the Party. We hoped that Hou Dachun would work hard for the party and seek welfare for the workers. However, during the national unity against Japan, he took advantage of his position as a representative of the workers to become a standing committee member of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, and even fraudulently solicited donations in the name of the association and put the money into his own pockets. If this is not corruption, then what is it? Our party is a party that seeks the welfare of the people, and all its members should be clean and self-disciplined, sacrificing themselves to help the people. If someone is taking from the people to benefit themselves, then even one item should not be taken. In recent years, some unscrupulous party members have either used the party's name to deceive others or have taken the opportunity to collect money. This is all due to the lack of enforcement of party discipline, and the party's reputation has declined as a result. The people have doubts about the party. When the association previously heard about Committee Member Hou's bribery and malpractice, we always thought it was a rumor fabricated by villains to slander him. Now, we have received a public statement from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation People's Association reporting the malpractice of embezzling 500 yuan in donations, with five pieces of attached evidence. If the matter is true, then Committee Member Hou's personality will be ruined, and the party's reputation will be completely destroyed. For the sake of the party's prestige, for the sake of eliminating social miscreants, for the sake of purging corruption among party members, for the sake of the future of the anti-Japanese national salvation, and for the sake of Mr. Hou's own personality, it is necessary to request that your esteemed association first suspend Hou Dachun from his duties and conduct a thorough investigation. If the above-mentioned facts are found to be true, then the regulations on punishing party committee malpractices should be invoked and the most severe punishment should be imposed. If the matter is slanderous, then it can be used as evidence to restore the party's reputation. Standing on the party's position, the association cannot remain silent. Therefore, we are submitting the public statement from the people and presenting it to your esteemed association, and we earnestly beg you to implement it promptly.

County Government Waives Taxes on Newly Governed Farmland 118

The County Finance Bureau Has Received Instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department

The Shanghai County Government is moving to Beiqiao, and the plans are currently being carried out in an orderly manner. All the newly governed farmland totals 52 mu, 6 fen, and 4 li, with a total annual tax of 6 liang, 1 fen, and 4 li of silver and 4 shi, 7 dou, 3 sheng, and 4 he of tribute rice. The County Finance Bureau reported the situation to the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department and requested that the provincial government exempt the grain tax. The provincial government then consulted the National Government's Ministry of Finance for verification. The Ministry of Finance stated that since the Provincial Finance Department had verified that the farmland was indeed taken for public use, the exemption from the grain tax should be approved. Yesterday, the County Finance Bureau received the transfer order from the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department, instructing them to comply with the order.

Raw Reeled Silk Mixed with Impurities 121

The Commodity Inspection Bureau Issues a Circular Banning the Practice

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry stated that the raw reeled silk produced by villagers is often mixed with impurities such as butter, lard, rice soup, paraffin wax, and sugar in order to increase the weight. In order to protect the quality of the silk, the bureau invited representatives from the silk merchants of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to the bureau to discuss solutions together. As a result, the representatives notified the silk firms in the interior of the evidence of adulteration found by the bureau and the negative impact of the practice, and urged them to strictly comply with the regulations. After the discussion, the staff of the Silk Inspection Department of the bureau baked the dry silk that had been mixed with sugar or Bletilla striata in front of the representatives, and the color turned yellow as expected. Then, the bureau staff led the representatives to the chemical testing department to test the previously baked yellow dry silk in person, and it was also proven to be mixed with bran. In order to implement the supplementary resolutions, the bureau has recorded the case and sent a letter to the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Merchants Association, requesting that they take note of the matter and handle it accordingly.

Fire Alarm During the Day on Henan Road 123

Three Stores Suffer, Losses Amounting to Hundreds of Thousands

A fire broke out at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Henan Road yesterday afternoon. The victims were Xihongtang Stationery Store, Runxiangtai Leather Goods Store, and Yangqinghe Fuji Jewelry Store, with enormous losses. The fire started around 12:30 PM. The store employees were preparing for lunch when the fire suddenly descended. No. 406 Xihongtang, No. 405 Yangqinghe, and No. 407 Runxiangtai were all engulfed in the vortex. At that time, the fire seemed to have started from the second floor, so the buildings facing the street and those in the back were spared. The fire was very fierce at the time, with thick smoke spreading everywhere and flames flying wildly, making it impossible to approach. The Central Fire Department, which was nearby, immediately dispatched vehicles after hearing the news and tried its best to put out the fire. After about half an hour, the fire was brought under control. At that time, it was around 1:00 PM, the time when traffic on Nanjing Road and Henan Road was most congested, and traffic was temporarily cut off. After the fire was extinguished, the fire department sent personnel to guard the area, fearing that the remaining embers would cause further damage, and did its best to protect Dalun and Junfeng, so that they would not be affected. Afterwards, it was learned that Runxiangtai suffered the greatest losses, followed by Yangqinghe and Xihongtang. The total loss was estimated to be tens of thousands of yuan. Dalun and Junfeng suffered only slight water damage and were also greatly frightened.

Three Major Parts of the Riyue Bank Case Appeal 124

(1) The Issue of Responsibility of Ye Shantao and Others

(2) The Issue of Attorney's Fees for Lawyer Tan Yigong

(3) The Issue of Living Expenses for the Huang Family

After the collapse of the Shanghai Riyue Bank and the Great World Tourism Savings Department, Pan Zhaobang and others were appointed by the former French Concession Court to liquidate the assets. On the one hand, the plaintiffs' claims against Ye Shantao and other directors and shareholders were rejected. Therefore, the creditor's agent lawyers Yan Luqing, Dong Yu, Dong Chi, Bian Jialu, Xu Yannian, Chen Zhigao, and Zhou Xiao'an jointly represented the creditors and stated their dissatisfaction by filing a petition with the former French Concession Court for review. (According to the former French Concession Court, only a review could be requested, and there was no appeal mechanism.) Later, because the National Government took back the public courts, the Higher Third Branch Court was established, and the former case was transferred for trial. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, Zhao Zhenhai, a prosecutor from the Higher Third Branch Court, sat in the civil court for the trial. He first asked Lawyer Yan and others about the total amount of debt and lawsuits. He also said that lawyers Wu Jingxiong and Jiang Yiping were representing the 3,386 creditor households of Jing Xiren and others, and they had also filed an appeal to confirm the responsibility of the directors and shareholders. The court had already summoned them once. He asked whether the lawyers in question were also going to file an appeal in this case, or whether they would wait for Jing Xiren and others' appeal to be resolved and then handle the matter in accordance with the resolution. Lawyer Yan Luqing said that before the 3,000-plus creditor households of Jing Xiren and others filed a lawsuit with the First Special Court, they had only participated in the French Concession Court. The judgment of the former French Concession Court was based on the request of the lawyers involved. This appeal was based on the arguments of the lawyers involved. It was stated that Jing and others' appeal was after their appeal. Now, the lawyers involved were requesting a consistent appeal. The official then asked the lawyers which of the three major parts of the judgment they were dissatisfied with. Lawyers Dong Yu and Xu Yannian replied: (1) The issue of the responsibility of Ye Shantao and other directors and shareholders; (2) The attorney's fees of 20,000 yuan for lawyer Tan Yigong, the representative of the Huang family, which was awarded by the former French Concession Court. This amount was deducted from the debt, and the creditors were not willing to accept it; (3) The Huang family's request for 60,000 yuan in living expenses, of which 40,000 yuan was awarded by the former French Concession Court. The creditors also opposed the deduction of this amount from the debt. Therefore, they were requesting an appeal. The official then asked whether the judgment of the former French Concession Court was final. The lawyer replied that the former French Concession Court only relied on the court's order as the final judgment and there was no written judgment. At this point, Judge Zhao ordered the creditor's agent lawyers to submit detailed reasons for the appeal and the total amount of the lawsuit within 20 days and to pay the litigation fees before the case could be heard again.

The Case of Plotting to Murder Her Husband - Not Accepting the Life Sentence 125

Zhu Zhang Appeals

The Testimony of Each Witness Remains the Same

Zhu Shisheng, the owner of Nanyang Department Store, located at No. 100 Yangshuo Road, who was a local resident of 53 years of age, had an argument on July 24 of this year at 6:00 PM with his step-wife, Zhang, who was 38 years of age, over the funeral arrangements for his unmarried daughter, Si Mei, who was born to his first wife. He was beaten and injured. He was later sent to Tongde Hospital at No. 1 Tongfu Road for treatment, but he died the next morning at 2:00 AM. The Yangshupu Police Station dispatched detectives to arrest Zhu Zhang and brought her to the First Special District Court, where she was sentenced to life imprisonment. Details have been reported previously. Because Zhu Zhang did not accept the sentence, she hired lawyers Lin Qing and Chen Zemin to file an appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Chief Judge Song Yuan and Judges Du and Ye came to the First Criminal Court for investigation. According to the appellant Zhu Zhang's statement, she had been married to Zhu Shisheng for 19 years, and the case was a complete miscarriage of justice. At 6:00 PM on that day, after the daughter's funeral, everyone was drinking in the parlor. Those present included the neighbor Qiu Songlin, the shop employee Chen Jiying, the relative Yang Changlin, her brother Zhang Changsheng, and her nephew Zhang Heshang. At that time, a group of hooligans suddenly arrived outside. Her husband, upon hearing the news, left his seat and went out to call for help. He was also knocked down by those people, who then fled in a rush. She helped him up and sat him on a stool. She was about to go to the police station to report the incident, but her son-in-law, Zhang Xinglin, said that he would go instead. After a while, he returned and told her to go herself, so she went to the police station to report the incident. When she returned, her husband had already gone upstairs. He said that his body was numb, so she used brandy to rub his chest. Later, he was sent to the hospital, and she went with him. The doctor said that his brain vessels had ruptured. If there was no danger within three days, his life could be saved; otherwise, it would be ineffective. When her husband was dying, she was also by his side. Her son-in-law, Zhang Xinglin, falsely accused her of having an affair and making trouble out of nothing. She asked the court to investigate the matter and stated that she did not beat her husband. She begged for justice. Then, Zhang Heshang testified that Zhu Zhang was his aunt. On that day, it was for his cousin's funeral, and he was also drinking in the parlor with everyone that evening. There were seven people in total. His uncle (the deceased) and Zhu Zhang's brother said that they were fortunate that everyone was present, otherwise the coffin for his daughter would have been difficult to make, which was a sign of domestic unrest. As they were speaking, his aunt (the appellant) suddenly came in from the store and questioned them. His uncle, fearing her, told her to ask her brother. A quarrel and fight then ensued. His uncle ran outside and was dragged back in by his aunt. His uncle called for help and did not fight back, but he did not know where he was injured. At that time, his uncle took a few steps and sat down on the stool, saying that his body was numb. Later, he was helped upstairs, and Zhang Heshang followed him. At that time, his uncle was still able to speak and asked his son, Miaofu (born to the appellant), whether he wanted copper coins. Then, he closed his mouth and did not say anything more. However, when he was being beaten, his uncle suddenly squatted down, and his aunt picked him up. He did not see hooligans arriving and beating him. Then, the shop employee Chen Jiying testified that he was from Changzhou and had been working in the store as an accountant since April of last year. On that day, for the funeral expenses of Si Mei (Zhu Shisheng's daughter), Zhang was determined to reduce all expenses, which led to a dispute. After Mr. Xu mediated, the matter was settled. After the funeral, that evening, when all the relatives and friends were drinking, Zhu Shisheng said to Zhang's brother and others that he was fortunate that they were present today, otherwise his daughter's coffin would not have been able to go out, which made Chen very angry. Zhang entered from the store, and Zhu Shisheng said, "Do you want to slap me in the face?" (The white-eyed person is Zhu's sister). A quarrel and then a fight ensued. Zhu called out "Good!". At that time, someone punched Zhang Heshang. Zhu said that it was none of their business and that it was a quarrel between husband and wife. After a while, Zhu squatted down and called for help, and Zhu Zhang picked him up. Zhu then went outside. At that time, there were many people, and Chen could not see clearly. In the past, the couple often did this. Then, Zhu Shaoying testified that she was a neighbor. At that time, after Zhu Shisheng and Zhu Zhang had an argument, Zhu Shisheng asked a shop apprentice to invite her to scrape his skin to relieve the pain. When she arrived, Zhu said that his legs were numb and he had a headache. She examined him and found that it was not a skin problem, but she rubbed his chest a few times. Later, he scraped his skin himself. Then, Yuan Abao testified that he was a watermelon seller near Zhu's store. At that time, he heard Zhu and Zhu Zhang fighting and saw Zhu running out, wearing slippers. Zhu Zhang pulled him back in and touched his lower part with her right hand. Zhu then fell backwards and called for help, with his eyes rolling back and not saying anything. At that time, Zhu Zhang was shirtless and had a fierce expression, as if she was going to perform some kind of exorcism. When Chen Jiying was questioned, he said that he did not see Zhu Zhang shirtless. He heard Zhu calling for help outside, but not inside. Zhang Heshang also said that Zhu Zhang was wearing a short shirt inside, but he did not see what she was wearing outside. The appellant's lawyer requested a postponement, stating that there would be witnesses arriving for the next hearing. He also stated that since the case occurred, the appellant's store had been closed and that no one was in charge of the money and other matters. He also said that the deceased's coffin was still in the store because the case had not been concluded. For the sake of caution, he requested that the court seal the coffin and store it elsewhere. Chief Judge Song ordered that the case be investigated again and rescheduled for a hearing. The coffin was to be marked and placed elsewhere first.

Butcher Kills Wife 126

Wife Unwilling to Stay at Home, Husband Angered and Acts

A woman named Qin Zhang, 32 years old, was from Haimen. She originally lived in her hometown but came to Shanghai on the 11th of this month. Her husband, Qin Shoufan, 34 years old, worked as a butcher at Chen Xinji's pig shop at 55 Yuezhou Road. After the couple met, Qin Shoufan, because he had cotton planted in his hometown, ordered his wife to return home on the 13th and gave her 30 yuan for household expenses and travel funds. However, the woman was naturally licentious and unwilling to return. She cohabited with Fan Shougen, who lived at 50 Jiaxing Road. Her husband received a letter a few days ago, learning that his wife had not returned home. He found her at Fan's house, dragged her out, and took her to the home of his brother, Zhou, at 3248 Puanfang, Zhoujiazui Road. An argument erupted. Qin, in his anger, grabbed a butcher knife from his brother's house and stabbed the woman in both thighs. She fainted from the pain. Qin then went outside. His sister-in-law, Qin Zhu, saw this and screamed. The neighbors heard and reported it to the Chinese police at 2288 and to the Harbin police station, who dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. When they arrived, the woman was already dead. They carried the body to the autopsy room on Feilun Road and arrested Qin on Yuezhou Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Li, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong, a clerk, and others, to the morgue to examine the body. The court convened, and Qin Zhu testified that her husband was out at the time. Only she and her child were at home. She did not witness the argument. Qin Shoufan testified that he was at his brother's house and wanted to ask if she had spent the money. She tried to stab him with a knife, but it fell to the ground. He picked it up and stabbed her twice. He only intended to scare her and did not mean to kill her. After hearing the testimony, Mr. Li declared that the deceased, Qin Zhang, was indeed stabbed to death by her husband, Qin Shoufan. The police have filed charges against the murderer. He will be tried by the court according to the law. The body was returned to Qin Shoufan for burial after he signed a guarantee. The knife was kept as evidence.

Xu A'mei Judgement 127

Sentenced to Ten Years and Six Months

Xu A'mei, a local resident living at 496 Kangti Road in the French Concession and a committee member of the French Tram Workers' Union, was previously arrested by the French police for inciting a strike. Anti-government books and leaflets were found in his home. He was sent to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The police filed charges according to the law. After repeated interrogations, the trial concluded, and a verdict was scheduled. Yesterday, the verdict was delivered. At 3 PM, Judge Guo Dezhang, along with assessors Zhang and Li, and Prosecutor Zhang, went to the First Criminal Court and ordered the defendant to be brought before the court. After questioning his age, occupation, origin, and address, the verdict was announced. Xu A'mei was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment and twelve years of deprivation of civil rights for organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. He was also sentenced to three years of imprisonment and three years of deprivation of civil rights for interfering with public electrical services. He will serve a total of ten years and six months of imprisonment and twelve years of deprivation of civil rights. The number of days of detention before the verdict is final will be counted as two days for each day of imprisonment. The books and leaflets seized in the case will be confiscated.

Furthermore, it is reported that the Chinese and French authorities, in order to prevent further unwarranted strikes and disruptions to public order, are preparing to dismiss seventeen workers in the factory who had been in contact with Xu A'mei and were known to be troublemakers.

Social Affairs Bureau Bans China-America Bank 136

The China-America Bank on Guangdong Road has not registered with the competent authorities according to the law. It is now rumored that it intends to issue high-interest dividend bonds to absorb funds from ordinary people. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, based on reports, has banned it. It is learned that the bureau's order to the company is as follows: "Order to comply. According to reports, the company has recently issued a type of non-convertible paper money called 'High-Interest Dividend Bonds,' with a total value of 250,000 yuan. Each bond is sold for one yuan and will be redeemed after five years. The bond, explanatory brochure, and articles of association have been forwarded. It has been found that merchants who operate savings businesses without being approved and registered, and who take advantage of social weaknesses to absorb small savings from ordinary people with high-interest rates and prize incentives, have been strictly banned by this bureau in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Industry. The company was previously ordered to register within a time limit but has not yet applied. Recently, it has re-issued High-Interest Dividend Bonds, which is inappropriate. It is ordered that the company immediately apply for registration and redeem all issued High-Interest Dividend Bonds within fifteen days, and submit a plan for closure for review and approval. This matter concerns social finance and must not be neglected, lest you incur guilt. This order is imperative."

He also presented sufficient proof. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Xu ordered that Hong Jingshan, Wang Xiting, and Cao Deyu be released on bail, while the remaining defendants were returned to custody. If No Money is Given, Then Provide Eternal Support

Sun Miao also stated that if the defendant was unwilling to pay the requested compensation, she, her young daughter, and her aunt would have him support them forever. Judge Shen had both sides' lawyers debate and ordered the defendant to be returned to custody for a scheduled verdict.

Discovery of Ancient Herbal Manuscript in the Dunhuang Stone Chamber 143

The ancient herbal manuscript in the Dunhuang Stone Chamber, originally named "Dietary Therapy Herbal," was written by Meng Xian of the Tang Dynasty and specifically discusses methods of nourishment to be offered to Empress Wu Zetian of the time. Meng studied under Sun Simiao and served in the palace, so his experience and knowledge were superior at the time. His "Dietary Therapy Herbal" was further annotated and revised by Zhang Zengbei and more than ten others, increasing its value. However, due to the chaos of the times, the original manuscript was lost and no longer existed, which was a misfortune for Chinese medicine. Unexpectedly, ancient books from the Tang Dynasty were found in the Dunhuang Stone Chamber in Gansu at the end of the Qing Dynasty, and the "Dietary Therapy Herbal" was among them. In 1907, British explorer Dr. Stein heard this news during an expedition in the Western Regions and tracked it down. He collected ancient books, loaded them up, and left, and they are now stored in the British Museum in London, so the Chinese people cannot see the "Dietary Therapy Herbal." Recently, a Chinese man, Zhang Hongming, managed to copy the original manuscript and return it to China for printing. It includes a title by Mr. Cai Yuanpei, Director of the Academia Sinica, and a preface by Mr. Zhao Yaonong, Director of the Chinese Medicine Research Department of the Academia Sinica. The book is bound together and priced at one yuan. It is sold at the Commercial Press and the Great East Book Company on Fourth Malu Road in Shanghai.

Pan Yishan Accused by Wife 148

Bigamy, Abandonment, Abuse, and Other Crimes

Requesting Divorce and Alimony

Wang Ying, a woman from Yunnan, is twenty-three years old, beautiful, and has received a secondary education. In the spring of the 13th year of the Republic of China, Ms. He Xiuzhen, a classmate of Wang's mother, got married in her hometown and hired Pan Yishan, a fellow villager, as the wedding officiant. Wang served as the bridesmaid. Pan was then the Dean of Education at the Yunnan Military Academy and was thirty-eight years old. After an unexpected meeting with Wang, he took a liking to her. He entrusted a certain Mr. Liu, a brigade commander under Tang Jiyao, the former military governor of Yunnan, to propose to Wang's father. The proposal was accepted, and the wedding was held in the winter of that year, with Chief of Staff Shen as the officiant. The following year, Pan took Wang to live in Shanghai, renting a house at 93 Park Road in the Public Concession. For several years, the couple's relationship was close, and Pan held important positions in the military, such as Acting Garrison Commander of Wuhan, Commander of the Changsha Garrison, and Chief of Staff to Zhang Zongchang, etc. However, last spring, a rift appeared between them. Wang later discovered that he had secretly married another woman, which led to repeated abuse and abandonment of the family. Recently, she hired lawyer Li Ming to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing her husband Pan Yishan of bigamy, abandonment, and abuse, and requesting a divorce and alimony. The complaint stated that since marrying the defendant, the plaintiff's feelings were very deep. Last spring, the defendant went to the north alone, leaving the plaintiff in Shanghai for more than half a year. There was no news, and repeated inquiries were not answered, causing the plaintiff to be heavily in debt and almost everything mortgaged. Later, when the defendant returned to Shanghai, the plaintiff found a photo of the defendant and a young woman in his luggage. She immediately confronted him, but he became angry and violent. In August of this year, the defendant went to Qingdao, leaving the plaintiff in Shanghai, living in extreme poverty. Repeated requests for assistance were met with excuses, and the debt piled up. Now the defendant has returned to Shanghai from Qingdao, but he does not repay the debt and forces the plaintiff to go to Qingdao immediately, intending to harm her. When she argued with him, she was beaten. Recently, she found in the defendant's letter remarks such as "sent from Nanyang Road or Zhao's house," initially suspecting it was a relative, but later heard that the defendant had another wife and a daughter named Min, who is currently studying at Guanghua. Upon learning this, she was heartbroken. Since the plaintiff and defendant married seven years ago, she had hoped to grow old together, but the defendant acted against his conscience. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit, requesting that the defendant be summoned and punished according to the law, and ordered to pay RMB 4,000 for dowry and alimony. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiefen of the Fifth Criminal Court summoned the case. The defendant did not appear, but the plaintiff, Ms. Wang Ying, and her lawyer arrived in court. After stating the reasons for the lawsuit, Judge Xiao announced that the case would be adjourned and served on the defendant, ordering him to appear in court.

Zheng Yougen Assists and Causes Trouble

Wang Zubei's Life is in Danger

Wang Zhigang, a clerk of the First Special District Court of Jiangsu, lives at No. 1 Qingyan Alley outside Xiaonanmen in Nanshi. His wife, Hu, has a son named Zubei, who is sixteen years old. Shen Changgen, a Ningbo native, fifteen years old, lives with them. Shen and Zubei had a grudge over gambling, which led to frequent quarrels. At around 7 PM the other night, Zubei and Changgen had another argument over a trivial matter, which escalated into a conflict. Changgen could not resist and injured Zubei's head, causing blood to flow. At that time, Zheng Yougen, a relative of Changgen, happened to pass by and saw the situation. He immediately stepped forward and held Zubei's hands, making him unable to move. Changgen thought it was an opportunity and beat Zubei severely. Zubei's hands were held by Zheng, making him unable to resist. He was injured and fell to the ground, unconscious. His mother, Wang Hu, heard the news and rushed to the scene. She took Zubei to the hospital for treatment. It is said that the injuries were severe and his life may be in danger. In a state of panic, Wang rushed back and took Zheng Yougen and Shen Changgen to the police station of the First District to request punishment. The police chief ordered a preliminary hearing of the plaintiff and defendant. Because the case involved injury, he ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Shanghai District Court for investigation.

Jianghai Customs Burns Opium Yesterday 153

Jianghai Customs burned opium yesterday at the Customs Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong. Supervisor Ye Liangguang, representative of the police garrison headquarters, Huang Chen of the municipal government, Ju Zhijing of the First Special District Court, Lu Youchang of the Supervision Office, Zhou Chucai of the Anti-Drug Association, Wu Lintao of the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Cai Zanzhou, a member of the Third District, supervised a platoon of armed police to maintain order around the opium-burning kiln. Then Huang Yaoxuan, the representative of the chief of the Customs, Robert, ordered the workers to weigh, unpack, and verify the drugs. After confirming that everything was correct, the burning began at 9 AM and ended at 10:45 AM. A total of 7 dan, 20 jin, and 11 liang of opium were destroyed, valued at silver 77,748.58 yuan. In addition, 1,226 liang of morphine and 2 dan and 22 jin of poppy shells were burned. There were also drug pills containing morphine, with a total value of 4,345.8 yuan. The above-mentioned contraband was seized by Customs officers on various ships during the three-month period from July 21 to September 20 this year.

"The End of Extraterritoriality in China" Published Soon 160

Dr. Thomas F. Millard, an American advisor to the National Government, has supported China's efforts to abolish unequal treaties. Recently, he wrote "The End of Extraterritoriality in China." The writing is concise, comprehensive, and divided into four chapters: (1) China's announcement of the abolition of extraterritoriality, (2) the background of extraterritoriality, (3) the process of China's failed negotiations to abolish extraterritoriality, and (4) expectations for the future. The appendix includes more than ten documents related to extraterritoriality, including official documents, reports, and research findings, which are essential reading for those studying political science and international law. The section on suggestions regarding the future of Shanghai is a critique of Judge Feetham's report on the situation in Shanghai and is an indispensable reference for those concerned about the future of Shanghai. The book is approximately 50,000 words in length and has been translated into Chinese by Xu Fushan with the consent of the author, Dr. Millard, and the Minister of Foreign Affairs. The translator has added notes and supplementary materials, making the translation no less valuable than the original book. It is said that it will be published soon.
