Reader Correspondence: Mr. Yin Donglin 162

(Not Selling Japanese Goods Results in Good Business Performance)

I am a small shop assistant at a counter. Seeing the repeated failures of the boycott of Japanese goods in the cloth industry, I was outraged and, after returning to the store from participating in the citizens' assembly, contacted my colleagues to voluntarily boycott them, which has yielded good results. I am very satisfied, so I am publishing the facts and asking my colleagues to voluntarily boycott them. I am a shop assistant working in a cloth store near the ancestral Chuan Cun Memorial Tower of the Rinan Yarn Factory in the western district. Since the violent Japanese forcibly occupied the Northeast, Japanese warships have been densely deployed in the Yangtze River basin, and the national situation is extremely dangerous. Appealing to justice has been unsuccessful, and relying on force is insufficient. The only thing we can rely on is the thorough boycott of Japanese goods by the Chinese people. However, from the May 9th, May 3rd, May 4th incidents to the Wanbaoshan Massacre, none of them are not deeply engraved in the hearts of the Chinese people, and after each tragedy, the Chinese people have to carry out an anti-Japanese movement. Originally, the violent Japanese plundered no less than 300 million yuan from our country every year to make up for their economic panic and help their unemployed workers. If the Chinese people, from top to bottom, were determined to boycott and persist to this day, the violent Japanese economic situation would definitely undergo major changes, and factory closures and increased unemployment would be expected. Unfortunately, the five-minute heat of the Chinese people has not arrived, and the clouds quickly dissipate, and the boycott results are only equal to zero. Even in my cloth industry, except for some western goods, 70% of the goods are enemy goods. Japanese merchants, seeing that our country has repeatedly boycotted them, have not been unaffected, and they have used many cunning schemes to impersonate western merchants, mixing imitation pearls with real ones to deceive the Chinese people. Ordinary cloth produced by our factories mostly uses 60-count and 42-count double-stranded yarn, which are mostly Japanese goods. Occasionally, one or two domestic yarn factories work hard to operate, but the supply cannot meet the demand, and the colors are inferior, so the weaving industry unanimously competes to purchase Japanese raw materials. It can be seen that the economic aggression of Japanese imperialism has been deeply rooted. Reading your newspaper's message from Mr. Fusheng, the counter staff in the cloth industry are restricted by the power of capitalists and cannot move freely, which affects their livelihoods. This is indeed a difficult question for more than 10,000 shop assistants in Shanghai to answer. Originally, ordinary shop assistants in the cloth industry do not have the same enthusiasm as school students for saving the country. Except for a few who pay attention, others are still the same as before, as if it has nothing to do with them. This has lost the national duty. If they continue to sell enemy goods and fool their compatriots for the benefit of capitalists, then they are truly willing to be cold-blooded animals. Therefore, at the beginning of the anti-Japanese movement, I myself swore that I would not sell enemy goods to my compatriots "such as enemy goods, floral plain contribution呢, satin, moon glory 羢, fine cloth···etc.," which are all major sales items in the cloth industry in winter. Customers cannot easily distinguish them. If they insist on cutting a certain kind of cloth, it is difficult for the shop assistants to deal with it. I point out that this is enemy goods and advise them to buy domestic goods. At first, the capitalists and colleagues ridiculed me, but I argued that everyone knows about the boycott of enemy goods this time, so I went a step further to discuss voluntarily sealing them up and declared that we would not buy or sell them. (1) It can enhance the credibility of the store, (2) It can gain the trust of customers. I repeatedly persuaded and discussed with the capitalists and shop assistants in detail, and finally it was passed. Unexpectedly, since the implementation, in less than half a month, the business has become more prosperous. Now both labor and capital are very satisfied, but it also relies on the propaganda of schools and news organizations to make it easier for customers to persuade them to buy domestic goods. Overall, if my cloth industry does not import Japanese goods, it will not necessarily close down. Now there are many cloth industries in Shanghai and other major commercial ports that have voluntarily boycotted or established anti-Japanese associations to seal them up. However, colleagues in inland towns and villages have not thoroughly understood and secretly smuggle and repackage them in parcels, destroying anti-Japanese work. Are they willing to be slaves of a fallen country? Enthusiastic shop assistant comrades, you have encountered difficulties at the counter, of course, are the same. Who is willing to lag behind in loving the country? I urge everyone to inspire their conscience, follow my suggestion, enlighten the public, be bold, and never use Japanese goods. My cloth industry will never close down. Boycott them quickly!

Free Talk

Voice of Resistance

— Zizai

Japan was originally called the Wanu (dwarf) Kingdom. It changed to its current name at the beginning of the Xianheng period of the Tang Dynasty. During the Hongwu period of the Ming Dynasty, Japan sent an envoy, Hali Maha, to submit a memorial and make purchases. Emperor Taizu asked about their national customs. Hali was arrogant and conceited, and presented a five-character律 poem: "Our country is like the Central Plains, our people are like the ancients. Our clothing follows the Tang system, our rites and music follow the Han dynasty. Silver urns hold clear wine, golden knives slice plain carp. Every year in February and March, peach and plum blossoms bloom naturally." Emperor Taizu hated his rudeness, rebuked his absurdity, and rejected his tribute to show his abandonment. In recent decades, Japan has been violent and reckless, repeatedly invading our country. Its cruelty and evil are unacceptable to reason and humanity. There is a Cantonese saying: "A man is not four feet tall, but hides a knife in his belly." Now, looking at the violent acts of the Japanese dwarfs, I believe it even more. However, those who commit many injustices will inevitably destroy themselves. This is what history tells us. Will the Japanese dwarfs realize this?

Thoughts on Eliminating Garden Weeds

— Zhai Fu

Wen Shou (Celebrating a Birthday) 165

In the winter of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, a group of older children worked in Kaifeng, which could also be said to be playing. Because they found joy in their work and significance in their play. One day was Mrs. Cha Mianzhong's birthday, and Zou Bingwen suggested a new way to celebrate her birthday. This new method was to put the wife's photo in the quilt overnight. Mianzhong said, "I didn't bring a photo, what can I do?" Bingwen said, "Then writing her name will also work." Whether Mianzhong did this is unknown. But this kind of innocent life is worth appreciating.

Now Mianzhong is helping with the flood relief, suffering with the hungry and drowning, and unable to rest. Bingwen is in charge of judicial administration and is concerned with agricultural research. They are now adults with many thoughts. In their spare time, recalling the children's games of the past can reduce their worries. Good, let us revive as children together!

The Old Trick of Annexing Korea 166

— Xu Jie

Korea was a dependency of our country. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, Toyotomi Hideyoshi of Japan claimed to be guarding the country and invaded the Korean capital. The Koreans hated him. When Daewongun was in power, he burned the Japanese embassy. Japan accused him and demanded 500,000 yuan in compensation and permission to build a military guard embassy. At that time, the Korean officials were divided into two factions. One faction, led by Min Young-ik and Min Young-jun, advocated relying on China and adhering to the principle of serving the great. The other faction, led by Hong Young-sik and Kim Ok-gyun, advocated relying on Japan and pursuing independence and reform. They attacked each other, causing internal strife. This allowed Japan to reap the benefits. In 1894 (the twentieth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty), the Donghak Party rebelled in the country. Japan used the pretext of protecting merchants and sent troops to Korea. The Korean king sent an envoy to the Qing court to request troops. The Qing court ordered Admiral Ye Zhichao and Nie Shicheng to lead troops to Asan. When the Donghak Party saw the arrival of the Chinese and Japanese troops, they dispersed. Thus, the internal problem of Korea became an international negotiation between China and Japan. After Japan defeated Russia, it made Korea a protectorate. According to the agreed terms, Japan was allowed to station troops in Korea and establish military police. The Japanese envoy Ito Hirobumi forced the Korean king to abandon his diplomatic powers and established a protectorate in the Korean capital, establishing branch offices in each province and placing police at the gates of the Korean imperial palace to monitor the comings and goings of his ministers. The Korean emperor was very angry and secretly sent Lee Sang-seol, Lee Wee-jong, and Lee Joon as representatives to the International Peace Conference in The Hague to complain. The International Peace Conference refused to consider the proposal. The secret envoys returned discouraged. They also secretly appealed to the US government, but were refused a meeting. Several days later, someone using an American name sent a telegram to major newspapers in various countries stating that the Korean emperor was now imprisoned by the Japanese police, almost like a prisoner. The Japanese were furious and forced the Korean emperor to abdicate. Korean officials, gentry, men, women, old and young, were all indignant and excited, like drunkards and madmen. A movement to boycott Japan arose. Rallies were held and speeches were given daily in the area around Zhonglu Cheondong outside the West Gate of Seoul. There were so-called Security Association, Independence Association, National Revival Association, One Heart Association, etc., which called upon members everywhere to grind their teeth, tear their eyes, pant, and run about. Some cut telegraph lines, some destroyed railways, some committed suicide, and some formed secret societies, but all were to no avail. Only Ahn Jung-geun's assassination in Harbin was somewhat gratifying, but Korea was ultimately lost to Japan. Alas, the frequent internal strife in our country today is like the factional disputes in Korea. Japan's invasion of the eastern provinces is like the invasion of Korea in the past. The unreliability of the League of Nations is like the unreliability of the International Peace Conference. The boiling public anger is like that of the Koreans in those days. Japan is using its old trick of destroying Korea. Will our country follow in the footsteps of the Three Hans? I am narrating the story of Korea's fall. I have no time to be sad for the Koreans. Alas.

World News Notes 167

— Haike

Sound Films in Court

Although sound films can only be used for entertainment, since the invention of sound films, they have been very helpful in practical applications. Now they are being used in court. Recently, in the Supreme Court of Melbourne, Australia, there was a lawsuit in which someone complained that the noise of a milk farm was disturbing the neighbors and asked the court to stop it. A sound film was presented to the court as evidence. The film recorded the sounds of the milk farm. After viewing the film, the judge found the complaint to be true and accepted the case. The plaintiff won the case. In the UK, sound films are often used in lawsuits related to sound. The Australian milk farm case has aroused the interest of British lawyers. It is expected that sound films will be used as evidence in other countries' lawsuits when necessary.

A few years ago, a tragic death occurred in the UK. A person died unexpectedly while filming. At that time, the camera happened to be working and completely captured his death. The film company presented the film to the court, which relieved them of legal liability. However, that was a silent film.

Lament for the Northeast 168

— Sun Choucheng

Ever since the Japanese army forcibly occupied the Northeast, the education sector has unanimously advocated inserting texts about the Japanese devastation of the Northeast into textbooks to awaken the youth. Yesterday, I received a letter from Yun'er, stating that Mr. Gong Ziyang, a history and geography teacher at Suzhou Middle School, recently composed "Lament for the Northeast," a piece of writing filled with grief. The school has adopted it as teaching material and is passing it on to the students. Therefore, I am transcribing the original text as follows:

Look at the Northeast, the atmosphere is filled with enemy forces. They indulge in greed and plunder, causing us worry and pain. They drove straight into the three provinces, sweeping across thousands of miles. The world is like this, where is justice to be found? What crime have we committed? They damaged their railway. The matter is trivial, but the situation is more wrong. One envoy had not communicated yet, and three armies were already deployed. Their hearts are those of tigers and wolves, harboring such intentions all along. The towering Zhang family, the pillar of the nation. The navy had giant ships, and the army was elite on land. Yet they did not focus on border affairs, instead engaging in internal strife. How could they suddenly let the enemy run rampant? It was said that there were international bodies that could be sought for intervention. To lose our pillar of the nation, with a single dispatch. It was thought national difficulties could be eased and the enemy's situation could be intimidated. How did this matter end? Heavy troops have been holding it for a long time. Since the defeat of our army, the people are terrified. Like stray dogs, like lost sheep. Mountains and rivers change color, the sun and moon lose their light. A great mistake has been made, how can it be remedied? The towering Shenyang, the former residence of emperors. Tall pavilions with three levels, wide streets open in all directions. Scholars and women are stranded in vain, wealth and goods are piled up like mountains. Overnight, banners and flags have changed. Swift as wind and lightning, sweeping across the entire Liaoning. Loss and destruction have a date, but when will restoration come? Mr. Li is in a tight spot, Su Wu's spirit has vanished. They temporarily remove their old clothes and pay homage to the new dynasty together. Border offices and provincial governments, the lives of the people are entrusted to them. What do they worry about, what do they scheme? Some flee, some are arrested. Joyful entertainment is hard to forget, but hardship and danger are ignored. The great rivers and mountains are entrusted to these children. Radio towers stand tall, airplanes soar. The stone archives are rich in books, and the Orchid Gears are equipped with good machines. Moving east and hiding west, with a hundred holes and a thousand sores. Working as a wedding dress for others, a fleeting spring dream. Railways are the lifeline of a nation. Once they benefited our travel, but now they serve the enemy's service. The poisonous flames spread further, and the national crisis becomes more severe. Millions of money, better to waste it in vain. Soon we will see outside the customs, where colonies are established wherever they go, taking our country's land and filling their family treasures. The avenues are filled with carriages and the road is paved, officials wear new clothes. They swagger through the city, with the majesty of gods. All sources of profit are occupied, and industry and commerce are driven away. No Manchus, no Han Chinese, wear similar clothing. The economy gradually weakens, and livelihoods are strained. Those who are fortunate enough to survive will forever be servants. Alas, how sad!

Mr. Liu Haisu's Reflections on His European Art Study Tour (Part 1) 170

— Ji Ping

The Oriental Cultural Society, organized and established in Paris by scholars from various countries in the Far East and Near East, has only seven years of history. However, the number of member countries has reached fifteen. The members who join are all people who have made considerable contributions in academics. It is not open to just anyone. The purpose of this association is: (1) to collect historical materials from various Eastern countries; (2) to examine and verify antiquities from various Eastern countries; (3) to study the different schools of thought in Eastern culture (such as language, art, religion, philosophy, etc.). After seven years of effort by members from various countries, it has achieved considerable results. Chinese members are the majority in this association. The first

President is also a Chinese member, Mr. Li Weihou. The mission he bears in Eastern academics and politics is very significant. Especially for the future of our nation and culture, he has a particularly significant influence. I attended a tea party of this association the day before yesterday and listened to the great theories of the scholars and the discussions on the progress of the association's affairs. I feel that its future contribution to Chinese academics and politics can be predicted to be extraordinary.

During the tea party, Mr. Liu Haisu, who had just returned from Europe after studying art, also gave a lengthy speech. He said that we are all muddleheaded in our own country. Once we arrive in Europe, we realize the brilliance of our ancient Chinese academics. We ourselves will not revive or promote them, but we let others absorb and explore them. In reality, we are deteriorating day by day, while others are making rapid progress. For example, in terms of art, Japan has taken some of our leftovers and pure Chinese paintings to Europe for exhibitions, expanding publicity and claiming them as national essence and representative works of Eastern art. Therefore, unless people who have studied Eastern art, the general public only knows that there is Japanese art in the East, but does not know that there is Chinese art.

He said that in recent years, various German states and universities have attached great importance to ancient Chinese academics, much more than we value Western academics. All universities have established Chinese academies dedicated to the study of Chinese culture throughout the ages. Chinese philosophy, literature, art, and various classics have been collected very comprehensively. Even Lao Tzu, Zhuang Tzu, Mo Tzu, Lie Zi, and the Confucian and Mencian doctrines have complete translations. This shows a glimpse of their research spirit. Universities are very welcoming of Chinese scholars to give lectures. However, the number of Chinese scholars who actually go to study and lecture is extremely rare. In mid-March of this year, when Mr. Liu arrived at the University of Frankfurt, the director of the Chinese Academy invited him to give lectures for three days. The first topic was "The Six Laws of Chinese Painting." When talking about the four words "Qi Yun Sheng Dong" (spiritual consonance), he gave the following explanation. Arrogantly, no longer suffering loneliness. I was alone on a journey, and scenes evoked my emotions. Leaning against the carriage, I silently recited Jiang Baishi's "South to North, What Is the Matter? Rippling Xiang Cloud Chu Water, My Eyes Are Heartbroken." I could not help but feel emotional. Fortunately, the journey was not far. At eleven o'clock, we arrived at the Pajiangkou Station. After getting off the train, we walked for about a mile to the riverbank. Lei Duan had hired a motorboat to wait and lead us. The crowd gathered, set sail, and advanced against the waves. We first went to Hidden Xia Cave. Climbing up winding cloud ladders and stone paths, the stream water was clear and gurgling. The temple was planted with flowers, red and purple and fragrant. Behind the mountain, there was a stubborn stone on which the words "Imperial Seal" were written. It is said to have been a stone seal left by Qianlong, but it is a false rumor and laughable. Turning west, we went to Flying Xia Cave. The magnificent palaces and halls were extremely grand. Twin peaks stand facing each other, forming lions and elephants. A magnificent spectacle. Behind the cave, there is a Phoenix Tower. In the evening twilight and the morning sun, the view from the railing is extremely beautiful. The person in charge here greeted us warmly and offered vegetarian meals to the guests. The vegetables were delicious and tasted better than home-cooked food. In the evening, we stayed in a small pavilion. The sound of the wind and waves vaguely entered our ears. I fell into a dream and felt like an immortal. The next day, I woke up at dawn and leaned on the railing to watch the sunrise. The morning clouds had not yet dispersed, and the morning sun was rising. The rays of light were colorful, making it impossible to look directly at them. After retreating and finishing breakfast, we bid farewell and went down the mountain. Walking slowly, there was still a lingering attachment. We still took a boat to Flying Come Temple. The temple was originally named Guangqing and is located in Yuxia in the upper reaches of Qingyuan. The mountains surround it, the river flows quietly, and the waves and sails are like entering a natural painting. Looking around, we washed away ten thousand loads of dust. Behind the temple, there is a flying spring hanging down like a white silk, making a slight sound as it hits the rocks. A Flying Spring Pavilion is built next to it. Looking up and listening to the waterfall, we could not bear to leave quickly. Celebrities such as Li Yinquan, Chen Shuren, and Pan Wenzhi often gathered with friends and lingered, forgetting to return. It is known that it is not a false name and has something particularly attractive. On the top of the mountain, there is also the Emperor's Shrine, the Reading Rock, the Returning Ape Cave, the Joy Rain Pavilion, and the Golden Lock Pool. Unfortunately, due to time constraints, we could not fully enjoy them. We will leave it for another day.

News from the publishing industry, the Pioneer Publishing House has just released the fifth edition of the "Compilation of Lyrics of Recorded Dramas," which includes the lyrics of new records from various record companies. It is also compiled in an eye-catching way, making it easy to browse. It is now being sold by Dasheng Gramophone Company and gramophone and clock stores in various places. I am grateful for the gift of one copy and hereby express my thanks.

Rotary Club of Storytellers

The Pestle of Knocking Dreams (19) 171

— Cheng Zhanlu

A gentle and pleasant wind blew towards us, interrupting Tao Chi's conversation! Looking up, we saw a large garden in front of us, with five large golden characters shimmering in the morning light – "Modern Paradise".

The three people's eloquence subsided, and they only proceeded towards this modern paradise. They couldn't remember many of the "Park Rules" posted at the entrance of the paradise, one on the left and one on the right. The most noteworthy rule was that it overturned the fallacy of "time flies like a river" and implemented a method to make youth eternal. People who entered it had no past and no future, only the present, only the everlasting and unchanging present.

The three people were attracted by the appeal of these park rules and couldn't help but enter this modern paradise without a past or future. The gentle and pleasant wind continued to blow, and the men and women in the park shuttled back and forth like weavers, their faces filled with smiles.

Tao Chi looked back at his companions, Zhao Meiting and Qian Lanxuan, but he didn't know when they had been separated. He didn't feel the loneliness of walking alone, because everywhere in this garden were his companions.

The chirping of the beautiful birds was so clear and crisp, and the rare flowers and exotic grasses were so fragrant and beautiful. The morning light was shining on the highest branch of the peach blossoms, which were just half-bloomed. The flower branch was reflected in a small pool of clear water, and the goldfish in the pool were playing with the flower shadows at the bottom of the water.

A soft singing voice was being sung in the pavilion. Looking from afar, they were all beautiful young women singing modern new songs. The alluring tones unknowingly intoxicated Tao Chi's spirit -

– Modern New Songs –

The Washington Conference is a barrier to peace;

The disarmament treaty is equivalent to abolishing war!

Moreover, there is also the League of Nations, the League of Nations,

The term "the strong eat the weak" will never apply in the twentieth century!

Compatriots! Don't worry, don't fret!

Here there are singing birds and fragrant flowers, here there is a gentle breeze and a beautiful sun;

Let us rejoice! Let us play!

Reasons for the Stagnation of White Factory Silk Sales 183

Disasters in various provinces are causing sluggish silk sales... Inventories are still high and sales have decreased significantly. In recent years, the domestic sales of new silk fabrics have been exceptionally strong, with a sharp increase in raw silk consumption. However, local silk prices are high, and various silk factories have come to Shanghai to purchase medium-grade Shanghai white factory silk for weaving high-quality silk fabrics. Therefore, the sales of factory silk fabrics have been quite active. However, since the floods in sixteen provinces, the domestic disasters have been severe, silk sales have been greatly reduced, winter silk orders have sharply decreased, silk inventories are very high, raw material consumption has greatly decreased, and the sales of Shanghai white factory silk fabrics have stopped. In the past one or two months, very few silk merchants from Hangzhou, Shaoxing, and Jiaxing have transacted in Shanghai white factory silk.

Shirting white velvet cloth remained stable, with 22 Jincheng at 6 taels and 8 maces, 13-pound electric cars at 10 taels, 15-pound electric cars at 11 taels, Double Rabbit at 10 taels, Double Fish Jiqing at 10 taels and 6 maces and a half, Double Bell at 7 taels and 9 maces and a half, and Three Bells at 8 taels and 4 maces and a half. Western goods, 1.6-foot printed velvet, were quite popular because eastern goods could not be sold. Anmao sold for 1 tael, 3 maces and 2 fen and a half, and Chongtai western satin was also extremely firm. Deji goods opened at 4 maces and 7 fen and a half.

Automobile News

Special Article 184

A Brief Overview of the American Automobile Industry in Late Summer and Early Autumn by Pei Gan 185

In the final month of this summer, July, the number of American automobile production was 221,485 vehicles. In August, due to Ford's production limitations, its production was also not as high as expected, with the quantity roughly around 155,000 vehicles. The recession in the automobile industry during the summer is about to come to an end. Before the end of the month, Ford announced its production volume as 50,000 vehicles. General Motors' production is expected to be 70,000 to 80,000 vehicles, with 60,000 vehicles being Chevrolet. Chrysler's July production was 25,000 vehicles. If the production and sales of the new streamlined models in August did not reach 37,000 vehicles, then its disappointment can be affirmed. The production volume of other parts of Chrysler is about 50,000 vehicles. Excluding Ford's production volume, adding the production of other car factories, the total automobile production in August should be around 155,000 vehicles.

Every year at the end of summer, the American automobile industry often experiences a decline. This is a normal phenomenon throughout the years and is not surprising. Therefore, although automobile production in July and August is so low, the factories are quite optimistic about the autumn market. This is because the autumn season is a turning point for automobile sales. Each manufacturer strives to sell at this time to promote the progress of their business. Based on the forecast for this year's situation, the sales of low-priced cars will have a greater advantage in the autumn. Manufacturers that produce low-priced cars, such as Ford and Chevrolet, are all rallying to save the sales of their products. Therefore, the overall automobile production in the United States in September will definitely exceed July and August, and the car manufacturing performance in the last quarter of this year will definitely be the best of the other three quarters.

Metabolism is the only key factor in the automobile business. Every new car that is released must use various methods to seek sales, and its replacement of old cars is even more important. However, if the market is weak and sales are not strong, then the fate of new cars will also be greatly affected. The new cars that came out in the American market this summer have been greatly affected by this. Therefore, in the past few months, the sales of new cars have been far less than the current situation. Recently, various businesses have had active turnarounds, and new cars have appeared, and their future is quite promising.

There is another matter that hinders current car sales, which is that each factory will have new models coming out. Buyers often postpone the purchase because the factories will release new cars in the early autumn. Therefore, those who intend to buy must wait for the new cars to come out before deciding on their purchase plans. For this reason, every year at this time, there is a period of transition. Sales of old cars have already been weak, while new cars have not yet been released. Therefore, there is a temporary standstill, and production and sales both tend towards a slump. As for the factories, they attach more importance to this matter. In addition to the need for demand, they do not allow excessive production to avoid stagnation. Instead, they use their remaining energy to manufacture new cars, so that when the new cars are released, they can develop on a large scale.

The new cars for next year are currently being rushed to manufacture by the factories. There has been a lot of progress in terms of innovation and improvement, and there are the latest plans that have never been seen in the automobile industry before, which will also be unveiled in the 1932 models. Most of these new cars cannot be sold at this moment and must wait until the beginning of winter to be released. When it comes to low-priced cars, the competition among factories next year will be even more spectacular. The factories that are currently manufacturing low-priced cars are already exhausting their efforts and planning day and night to manufacture their new cars in the most economical way, so that buyers can get the most practical means of transportation at the lowest possible price.

Regarding the promotion of new cars, the factories have also come up with various methods to seek urgent sales. Therefore, new cars have gradually appeared in the American market. However, their types are not very complete, and buyers are mostly waiting and seeing. Their intention is nothing more than to wait for all the new cars to be released before making a decision on which one to choose. Several factories have widely publicized the features of their new cars in order to promote their new models and have used methods such as discounts on old cars and low down payments to attract customers. However, the results have not been as satisfactory as expected, because buyers will not have the intention of replacing new cars until the beginning of winter. The biggest reason is that they must wait until the New York Auto Show next spring before deciding on their purchase plans.

Although there are currently no precise statistics on American car sales in September, experts estimate that it is approximately 180,000 vehicles, which is an improvement compared to August, but still low and insignificant. From September to December, the production and sales performance in October, November, and December will definitely be better than in the previous quarters. This is because the end of the year is approaching, and buyers are planning for next spring, so they will add new cars at this time. The new models of each factory will also be released gradually in these two or three months.

In addition to passenger cars, the sales of freight trucks have recently turned around. The factories have seen improvements in both production and sales. Therefore, the factories that specialize in manufacturing freight trucks are also quite optimistic about the future. The strong sales of freight trucks are often a precursor to the strong sales of passenger cars. Production and sales in August have verifiable records, and the bright future does not seem to be a lie.

Mr. Barris of the Owner's Mouth 187

Speed Higher Than Mail Car

The French Automobile Company, the Bombay dealer of Morris cars, recently received a letter from its customer, Mr. Brass, from Aparacheng, praising the excellent performance of the Morris car he purchased. The following is a partial translation of the original letter for the readers: "To whom it may concern. I purchased a Morris small car from your company on January 9, 1930, last year. It has been used for seventeen months now. Today, it took only nine hours to travel 365 miles from the Old Crow Children's Shop to Aparacheng, which means an average speed of more than 40 miles per hour. This is especially gratifying to me and I am happy to inform your company. I departed from the Old Crow Children's Shop at 1:30 p.m. on May 25 and arrived in Laizhou at 5 p.m., where I stayed overnight. What is most gratifying about this few hours of speeding is that when I departed from the Pingdian store, my friend happened to take the mail car to England. At that time, we bid each other farewell and agreed to talk again when the car arrived at Laizhou Station. At first, I thought my friend would arrive at the station first. Unexpectedly, my car arrived safely before the mail car. So I sat quietly and sipped tea, waiting for my friend to arrive. The next morning at 6:30, I continued my journey from Lai Station and arrived at Aparacheng at exactly 2 p.m. In total, the time spent resting on this journey was two hours. One was for breakfast at Jukulandu, and the other was to detour to Shagou to avoid the livestock. Apart from these two delays, the only unfortunate event encountered along the way was a slight puncture in the car tire. However, this had no effect on

Page 20

20-Year-Old Renault Car

Good Machinery Runs As Usual Renault Cars, a French manufacturer, are known for their beauty, precision, and fuel efficiency. People from all countries consistently praise them, and their global popularity is no accident. The car was placed by the wealthy maritime merchant Hadong and has been used for 20 years. It still runs completely as usual. Hadong took it for a walk every day when he was still alive. The long-lasting durability of the Renault car can be seen here.

Car driving is not related at all. It was not discovered until the morning after the end of the trip. Currently, all parts of the car have not been replaced, and the original tires are still in use and are still in good condition. In addition, what is especially worth mentioning is that this trip consumed a total of eight gallons of gasoline, which means that each gallon traveled 45 miles. As for the car's load capacity, although there was only one passenger, the rear of the car was fully loaded with luggage and sundries."

Youth Land

Physiology Class 189

— Jin

Whenever it was time for a boring lesson, there were always many classmates talking, making a fuss, and it was never quiet. Especially during physiology class, the newly arrived physiology teacher was extremely polite to the students, not very strict. It was really out of helplessness, because if the teacher said, "Hey, please be quiet," then there would be many impolite remarks offered, leaving the teacher unable to defend himself. Therefore, whenever it was physiology class, it was either talking or making a fuss, and very few people listened quietly. Even among those who seemed to be listening quietly, half of them were using novels as substitutes.

Among them, there was a Miss Mao who disliked the physiology teacher even more. During class, she always substituted with novels. She put the novel in the drawer, pulled the drawer open, leaned her body against the wall, and stared at the novel. A physiology book was placed on the desk. In this way, she could read steadily. If the teacher walked over, she would quickly close the drawer and cough a few times, as if preparing to start speaking.

One day, her novel was borrowed by a friend in the same room. Coincidentally, she encountered a physiology class she had no interest in. She then came up with a few difficult questions to ask the teacher. These questions were all outside the book. Later, she suddenly said, "Teacher, what are you talking about? Why can't we understand anything?"

"Then I'll explain it again," the teacher said slowly.

"No, teacher, you shouldn't speak in your local dialect. It's so unclear, it's really frustrating. Teacher, please speak Mandarin."

"Yes, Mandarin, but I speak Mandarin like this too."

"Then, what if we don't understand?"

"············"

In fact, although what he said was not pure Mandarin, it was very clear if listened to quietly. Miss Mao did not absolutely not understand, but for some reason, she always hated this teacher very much.

The class bell rang, and the teacher hurriedly walked out, as if escaping from hell. After the teacher left, Miss Mao said loudly, "Is this kind of teacher worthy of teaching us? Let's all go tell the Dean. Anyway, the Dean is very good to our class."

"I'm afraid it's not that easy," a Miss Zhuang quickly stood up and said.

"No, let's tell him that we don't understand what he's saying. It's impossible to listen to," Mao said angrily, "Then who is willing to talk to the Dean?" Miss Lu, who was sitting in the corner, quickly chimed in.

On the Lawn 190

— Bing She

Social News

The Conflict Between Chinese and Indigenous People in North Pekalongan by Qiu Bin Cun 191

"Where the sun shines, the British flag flies." This is the proud saying of the British. "Where the sun shines, there are Chinese living there." This is the honor we Chinese can have. The number of Chinese scattered across the five continents is estimated at ten million. We Chinese are endowed with the characteristics of hard work and endurance, and even more with a spirit of loving peace. Therefore, we Chinese have always been able to live an economical life peacefully under the rule of the government of our place of residence, without other ambitions. The economic power of the Chinese in various locations has also been at its peak for a time. However, since the Industrial Revolution in the seventeenth century, the industries of various industrialized countries have increased year by year. After the development of commercial capital in the nineteenth century, the capital of various industrialized countries has also increased year by year. By the time of the era of financial capital in the twentieth century, the various industrialized countries have even more problems of overproduction, overcapitalization, surplus labor, and economic panic. In order to solve the contradictions of their own surplus power and economic panic, capitalist imperialists have established various immigration regulations and the expulsion of Chinese. Recently, we have easily seen the expulsion of Chinese in Mexico, the expulsion of Chinese in Japan, and the expulsion of Chinese by local scholars in various colonies in the newspapers. The situation of the expulsion of Chinese by Koreans under Japanese rule is the most serious. Readers have already seen the facts about the Korean expulsion of Chinese in various domestic newspapers, so I will not repeat them. What I want to report to my compatriots here is the fact that the indigenous people of North Pekalongan in the Dutch and Portuguese East Indies are expelling Chinese.

1. Reasons 192

(1) The Dutch Commercial Gazette of Semarang has a record of the evil tide of expelling Chinese in North Pekalongan. According to the report of the North Pekalongan government, it is not yet said in detail that a brawl between Chinese and indigenous people occurred in front of the Kertod Mosque several months ago. The evil tide in North Pekalongan and the brawl in Kertod both carried the religious idea of expelling Chinese. In addition, Dr. Kramer, a Dutch official in North Pekalongan, established an indigenous middle-class society, which led to the anti-Chinese movement. The Dutch official himself could not save this crazy wave. In fact, if the local officials had advised the indigenous middle-class society not to use illegal means to compete with Chinese merchants in business last October or November, the disaster could have been prevented. This evil tide was entirely caused by the terrifying policies of various usurers. First, they spread the anti-Chinese color with religious overtones, and then Dr. Kramer incited them from behind, causing the anti-Chinese tide to break through and unable to bring it back on track.

(2) A dispatch from Batavia stated that North Pekalongan (state) in Dutch Java is a quiet small town on the north coast of Java. A long time ago, economic competition occurred between Chinese merchants and local people, so it has become an uneasy place. Many Chinese shops have announced their closure, and now they have reopened, but business is extremely deserted. They are still preparing to close at any time. After 5:00 p.m. every day, Chinese shops that are still open for business are as rare as phoenix feathers. Because of this, the retail industry has been greatly affected and has simply given European import wholesalers a great loss. As for the emergence of this economic enmity, it is because the local scholars wanted to establish retail sales to compete with Chinese shops, and later these shops sprang up like mushrooms after rain. The establishment of such shops in North Pekalongan and its vicinity all showed their sound organization and effective management, which gave Chinese small merchants a great blow. The customers of these local scholars' shops are mostly local scholars (Javanese). They are very loyal and would rather not buy the goods of Chinese shops even though they know they are cheaper. The losses suffered by Chinese shops in this business are unimaginable. Therefore, there are those who are unable to repay the debts of European import wholesalers, and those who threaten Europeans, saying that they must not wholesale goods to local scholars' shops anymore. The local government has tried its best to provide relief for this economic conflict, but it has been ineffective, and the Chinese authorities have been able to provide very little assistance to them.

From this point of view, we understand that the reasons for the expulsion of Chinese in North Pekalongan include religious discrimination and economic competition. In fact, there is also a hidden background of national struggles and the provocation of imperialists.

Two, Facts

The incidents of discord between Chinese and indigenous people in the North Pekalongan government, especially the various disputes that occurred in the city of North Pekalongan, are presented. The recent causes that directly triggered the riots, which led to the discord between Chinese and indigenous people, can be identified as coming from the following successive events:

(1) A Javanese from Cilimusni drove a truck and knocked down a Chinese peddler, Liu Yisun, on Ganbaran Street in North Pekalongan. The goods sold by Liu Yisun were scattered all over the road. Liu Yisun was furious and grabbed the truck driver to beat him. Just then, a barber named Simon, who came from Kajangan, stepped forward to help his compatriot and beat Liu Yisun back. From then on, many beatings continued to occur.

(2) Li Qingquan, who lived in Kajangan, was beaten by local people Rulacin and Zhaqimari.

(3) Liu Yisun, who lived in Kelimunan, was hit in the head with a sharp object by several local scholars.

(4) Li Shunyan was injured by three local scholars on Wenmai Street and sent to the hospital for treatment.

(5) Xu Chunzong was punched by several local scholars on Kelogelan Street at about 9:00 p.m.

(6) Zheng Zhenzhang, who lived in Walongyasen (belonging to the Madanglerhen district), was injured with a sharp object by two local scholars near Lanlongshali in the evening and sent to the hospital for treatment.

(7) Chen Jinsong was attacked by a local scholar named Zhasmali in Wanya Township. The murderer's record was filed.

(8) Huang Songshi was injured by a local scholar on the north street of Kelaya. The injury was serious.

(9) Huang Qingcai was carrying the Tua Pek Kong home and was hit in the head by several local scholars on Benchoer Street at 9:00 p.m.

(10) Shi Changfu, who lived in Banzhang Gulun, was punched by five local scholars on Wenmai Street. He spat blood and was sent to the hospital for treatment.

(11) Yan Zhaoneng, who lived in Jialengyare Township, was hit in the head by a local scholar on Basha Yare Street and sent to the hospital for treatment.

(12) Suli, who lived on Basha Yare Street, reported to the police that he was stoned into the house by local scholars in the evening.

(13) Shi Guiqing, who came from Wanyueshali, was hit in the right ear with an iron object by a local scholar on the tenth street of Kepuluo, causing it to bleed.

(14) The shop with He on Yajiaran Street was stoned into the shop by local scholars. The shopkeeper was hit by a stone on the back.

(15) Huang Yungui, the owner of the Longjing Railway Cafe, was injured in the hand by a local scholar in the station.

(16) Huang Qingtai was riding a bicycle and passing by Benchoer Street when he was suddenly attacked from behind by a local scholar, fell off the bicycle, and was injured in the head and shoulders.

(17) Shi Guixing was attacked from behind by a local scholar on Kepuluogan Street and injured his right hand. He was admitted to the hospital for treatment.

(18) Li Zhaoman, an iron merchant on Kepuluogan Street, was beaten by a local scholar named Laisted.

The following is a list of cases of Chinese people being beaten outside the city of North Pekalongan: (1) Cai Shengzhang was beaten by a local scholar named Zhasmali on Wu Ji'e Street due to a debt problem.

(2) Zheng Tianzhang was hit in the head and back of the head with a sharp object by a local scholar when he was riding a bicycle past Lanlongshali. The injury was quite serious.

(3) Xu Xingde was stabbed in the left ear and cheek with a sharp object by a local scholar in front of the Wu Yalan City Market and was admitted to the hospital for treatment.

(4) Chen Wuchun, who lived in Dido Township, reported to the police that he was stoned in his house by local scholars.

(5) Shi Juexun, who also lived in Dido Township, was injured in the lip by a local scholar named Huali.

(6) Su Ruishun complained to the police that he and Ye Qingdun were riding bicycles together when they were knocked down by a local scholar, causing the skin on both hands to be scratched.

(7) Huang Xiyuan encountered guerrillas in the countryside of Kedas and was asked by the guerrillas. He was frightened and ran away and was suspected of being a thief, so he was chased and beaten and injured and admitted to the hospital.

(8) Ye Baoyuan, the owner of a Waruliyalong shop, was surrounded and beaten by local scholars when he closed the shop at 8:30 p.m. that evening.

These are just reports of Chinese being injured by local scholars with bare hands or with stones and instruments in the past two or three months. Later, the methods became more and more violent, even changing from using sticks and blades to using guns and bullets to treat our Chinese.

Three, Appeals from the Chinese

The Chinese Consul and Vice-Consul in Semarang went to North Pekalongan to observe the local people, and requested the Consul to telegraph the Chinese government as soon as possible to send a warship to warn the Dutch government and save the Chinese in North Pekalongan from economic panic.

Moreover, in the economic competition between the Chinese and Javanese people, not only has the goods of the Chinese been resisted by the local scholars, but also the two sides often have conflicts, making the feelings even more broken and making the situation more and more dangerous.

Regarding the request of our Chinese to send warships for protection, the Dutch and Japanese newspapers in Batavia have commented on it, doing their best to ridicule, even saying that our country's warships are afraid of pirates. Such insults can indeed make us feel very embarrassed when reading them. Here, I will translate and publish the papers of the two newspapers. I don't know how the Chinese people will feel when they read them, and the National Government should also reflect on it.

The Dutch Daily News in Batavia and another Dutch newspaper criticized, saying that the Chinese in North Pekalongan have appealed to the Chinese government to send a large number of warships to North Pekalongan to protect the Chinese there. At the end, it was said that the Chinese warships must not dare to come to the Dutch East Indies because they are afraid of being attacked by pirates... etc.

In addition, the Japanese newspaper Yi Zhua Bang Ri Bao in Batavia criticized an incident in North Pekalongan. Here is an excerpt of its main points:

The conflict between the local scholars and the Chinese in North Pekalongan actually contains various very important meanings. As a result, they resorted to economic solutions. On the one hand, they dared to carry out a boycott-style closure, threatening the import merchants. On the other hand, the Chinese Consul-General directly negotiated with the Governor-General. Therefore, the most embarrassed were the Dutch import merchants, promoting the strict vigilance of the authorities. Now the Chinese in North Pekalongan are requesting the Consul-General to ask the Nanjing National Government for warships to come to the port to directly protect the lives and property of the Chinese there. In fact, the Chinese warships are now only on the banks of the Yangtze River, guarding against bandits and pirates, and have no time to send warships to Java.
